Chengdu is Not a Treaty Port and Should Not Have a Consulate According to the Treaty

(Nanjing) The establishment of consulates by various countries in our country is limited to treaty ports. Chengdu is not a commercial port and should not have a consulate according to the treaty. Previously, when Britain, Germany, and other countries found it convenient to negotiate, the Governor-General was allowed to send personnel to Chengdu temporarily under the name of consuls stationed in Chongqing, which set a bad precedent. Later, the personnel stationed in Chengdu by Britain and Germany were successively withdrawn. Only France still sends personnel with representative status to continue to be stationed in Chengdu. Over time, many people mistakenly regarded the French consul stationed in Chengdu as legitimate. In order to avoid misunderstandings from all sides, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs recently negotiated with the French Embassy, requesting that the title of consul used by the personnel be revoked to prevent other countries from following suit. The French Embassy has now agreed to instruct the personnel to change the title accordingly. (Special dispatch, 23rd)

(Nanjing) The establishment of consulates by various countries in our country has always been limited to treaty ports. Chengdu is not a commercial port and should not have a consulate. During the late Qing Dynasty, during the Guangxu era, the consuls of Britain and Germany stationed in Chongqing, speaking of encountering things to negotiate with the Governor-General, there was the act of sending personnel stationed in Chengdu under the name of consuls stationed in Chongqing. Later, the personnel stationed in Chengdu by Britain and Germany were successively withdrawn. France still sends representatives to continue to be stationed in Chengdu. Many people mistakenly regarded them as French consuls stationed in Chengdu. In order to avoid misunderstandings from all sides, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs recently negotiated with the French Embassy, requesting that the title of consul used by the personnel be revoked. It is now heard that the French Embassy has agreed to instruct the personnel to change the title accordingly. (Central News Agency dispatch, 23rd)

Preliminary Work Objectives of the National Economic Construction General Association; Developing Agricultural, Industrial, and Sideline Occupations; Promoting Thrift Movement

(Nanjing) The National Economic Construction Movement Committee General Association has selected the development of agricultural, industrial, and sideline occupations and the promotion of the thrift movement as the two major goals for practical implementation from the previously announced eleven preliminary work items. After the work is completed, other work will be promoted in order to achieve the effect of gradual completion and avoid the worry of achieving nothing by doing too much. According to Liu Weichi, the general director of the association, the development of agricultural, industrial, and sideline occupations will first require local branch associations to investigate the local agricultural, industrial, and sideline occupations and report to the general association. Then, the situation in various places will be statistically analyzed, and the best plans will be organized and implemented in order. As for the promotion of the thrift movement, it has been decided to consult with the New Life Movement General Association to cooperate. (Central News Agency dispatch, 23rd)

Various Businesses Request Postponement of Income Tax; Remarks by Gao Bingfang; All Concerns of Various Businesses Have Been Seen; Those Earning More Than 5% Profit Should No Longer Be Reluctant

(Nanjing) Various chambers of commerce have agreed in Shanghai to request the government to postpone income tax due to the decline of industry and commerce and the decline of all industries. Central News Agency reporters specially visited Gao Bingfang, Director of the Central Direct Tax Preparation Office of the Ministry of Finance, to inquire about his opinions. According to him, the various chambers of commerce have noted the poverty of the national economy and the sluggishness of industrial and commercial operations, and their conclusion to request a postponement of income tax is not without misunderstandings. The government has taken into account various points of concern to the various chambers of commerce in this income tax implementation and has taken steps to provide relief. Therefore, the provisional regulations on income tax clearly stipulate that all companies, shops, firms, factories, or individuals with capital of more than 2,000 yuan will be taxed only if their net profit after all expenses is more than 5% per year. Those with capital of less than 2,000 yuan are exempt from tax, and those with capital of more than 2,000 yuan but with a net profit of less than 5% per year are also naturally exempt from tax. This restriction on the starting point of taxation and the light taxation rate are intended to take into account the actual situation of the current social economy and the people's livelihood. Gao also said that income tax is equivalent to a congratulatory card from the store to my wealth. The government's implementation of income tax is hoping that every merchant can make money. Merchants who are willing to make money should not oppose the imposition of income tax. If they oppose the imposition of income tax because they have no wealth to make and their business can only barely maintain the status quo and there is no income to speak of, it is a great misunderstanding, because the government will not tax the income of those who cannot make money and whose income does not meet the legal conditions. Gao concluded by saying that a sound citizen who operates a business with a capital of more than 2,000 yuan and earns a net profit of more than 5% per year should not be reluctant to fulfill his minor obligations to the government. Moreover, the central government's purpose in implementing income tax this time is to reform the central tax system, equalize the burden on the people, and prepare for the finances of the extraordinary period. It is hoped that the business community will sincerely support it to see it through. (Central News Agency dispatch, 23rd)

(Hangzhou) As a result of the reorganization of the Zhejiang salt tax and the assistance of local governments in various counties in Zhejiang Province, income has increased sharply. New Life Movement General Association Bans Extra Tips at Tea Houses

(Nanjing) The New Life Movement General Association is aware that inns and tea houses in various places often ask guests for extra tips. This bad habit can help to foster extravagance and easily cultivate class consciousness among the people, which is contrary to the purpose of the New Life Movement. Therefore, it should be thoroughly reformed. The association has recently formulated implementation measures to ban extra tips and notified the New Life Movement Associations in various places on the 23rd to implement them earnestly. The main points of the measures are that no extra tips should be charged to guests in addition to the regular bill. If a tea house asks for extra tips, the guest should refuse. When a guest gives extra tips, the tea house should refuse. Otherwise, if it is found out, both parties will be punished. (Central News Agency dispatch, 23rd)

Rebel Army Launches Three-Pronged General Offensive; Decisive Battle Near Madrid in Spain; Cannon Fire Rumbles and Aircraft Carry Out Bombing; Government Forces Make Progress in Mixed Battles in Various Provinces

(London) It is heard that the Spanish government forces and the rebel army are currently engaged in fierce fighting outside Madrid. At dawn today, 5,000 militiamen rushed from Madrid to Guadalajara to stop the rebel army from advancing. Stores in Madrid are completely closed, and there are no pedestrians on the streets. (Reuters dispatch, 22nd)

(London) Although the Spanish government still claims to be defeating the rebel army, the fate of Madrid is still uncertain. It is heard that the rebel army is approaching the capital on three fronts. The first route is led by General Mola and is 36 miles from Madrid, and will soon come into contact with the government forces in the Boitaco highlands. Another route led by Mola has already started fighting in Villalba, and the third route will also press on towards Madrid. Government forces are currently preparing to meet them. (Reuters dispatch, 23rd)

France, Andaye The Spanish rebel army's three-pronged advance will come into contact with the government forces at the border between the provinces of Navarre and Guipúzcoa. The area is mountainous, rugged and difficult to traverse, and is very suitable for ambushes. There have been reports of cannon fire, and it appears the two sides have already engaged in a lull. However, the exact situation of the two armies is unknown. (Havas dispatch, 22nd)

Porras The rebel headquarters here announced today that the revolutionary army has decided to attack Madrid on Friday, at which time the outcome can be determined. The revolutionary army currently has 50,000 men and is only 35 miles from Madrid. Among them, 30,000 men are from General Franco's southern army, 10,000 men are from General Mola's northern army, and 7,500 men are imperial volunteer troops. They are currently surrounding Madrid on separate routes. Another team of fascist militia has reached 60 miles outside the capital today after engaging government-recruited miners. General Mola's forces, due to repeated military victories in the north, are preparing to step up their offensive on Madrid. Another rebel team is advancing from San Sebastian towards Irun, intending to link up with the rebel army advancing east along the French border. However, the rebel army advancing east has been unable to advance because bridges have been destroyed along the way. The two armies are aiming for northern Catalonia as their destination. There is also a third army composed of royalists, which is also advancing on Madrid. Its vanguard has already approached Madrid. General Mola originally planned to attack Madrid on Wednesday, but postponed it to await reinforcements. The rebel army in the San Sebastian area has also failed to completely control the area, which is another reason for the rebel army's postponement of the general offensive. (National News dispatch, 22nd)

France, Andaye The Spanish border is still sealed. Military news from the country is difficult to obtain, but looking from here, the cities are filled with smoke, and it seems that fires have broken out in many places. Many aircraft are flying back and forth over the mountains, presumably carrying out bombing. Cannon fire can be heard very clearly from the port of Bayonne. (Havas dispatch, 23rd)

Madrid The government broadcast a communiqué last night with optimistic wording, saying that efforts to restore national normalcy have been victorious. Government aircraft are currently bombing the rebel strongholds northeast of Madrid and can conquer them within 24 hours. (Reuters dispatch, 23rd)

Barcelona Bloodbath: Days of Hand-to-Hand Combat Leave Corpses Strewn Across the Field

Peppigran: According to a Reuters correspondent in Barcelona, the city has endured days of horrific hand-to-hand combat, day and night. Armed civilians assisted government troops in suppressing the rebels. The sounds of machine guns and cannons were constant. Sunday was one of the worst days, with at least 300 people dying in the streets by dusk. After the rebels were suppressed, anarchists and communists formed gangs, looting, burning churches and monasteries, and massacring priests. The Catalan government has declared that it now controls the entire province, and civic volunteer teams are heading to suppress the rebels in Zaragoza. (Reuters, 23rd)

琶塞龍納: The President of the Catalan Autonomous Provincial Government, 岡巴尼斯, has just ordered that the province's working class should immediately be formed into a militia to fight the fascist rebels, and has appointed 法拉斯 as the commander-in-chief of the labor militia. Last Sunday, a portion of the rebels occupied the local telephone bureau and several barracks. 法拉斯 himself led the militia to repel the rebels. In addition, 岡巴尼斯 also ordered representatives from each party belonging to the People's Front to form a committee to assist 法拉斯. This committee has now been established and has decided on the following: (1) to form patrol teams to execute the provincial government's orders; (2) every day after midnight, from 1:00 AM to 5:00 AM, no one is allowed to travel on the streets except for members of parties belonging to the People's Front. At this point, the provincial government is able to control the overall situation in Catalonia. Order in the city has been fully restored. All automobiles in the city have been requisitioned and are being driven by the police and the People's Front militia to patrol various locations and maintain security. Several airplanes have departed from here, heading to the southern Andalusian province, intending to bomb the rebels there. Air Force Colonel 桑蒂諾 was recently dispatched to lead a team to the city of Zaragoza, where they dropped bombs. A telegram has just arrived reporting to President 岡巴尼斯 that a total of seventy bombs were dropped, causing significant damage to the rebel barracks. The rebels also fired rifles and machine guns at the airplanes, but none were hit. This report has just been broadcast to various locations by the city's radio station. The city's volunteer troops are now preparing everything, waiting for orders to travel to the city of Zaragoza in trucks to suppress the rebels. (Havas, 22nd)

Three Hundred Fascist Rebels Sentenced to Death; Women Patrol Streets with Guns in the Capital

(London) One hundred fascist military officers and two hundred soldiers who recently rebelled in the Spanish capital were executed today. They were lined up against a wall and shot with machine guns. As the signal to fire was given, they all gave the fascist salute, facing death unflinchingly. (Reuters, 23rd)

(London) In Madrid, many Fascists still lie in ambush on balconies and in high-rise windows, sniping at pedestrians. The Spanish government declares that government forces have retaken Barcelona after fierce fighting, resulting in 500 deaths and 3,000 injuries. The Barcelona Air Force has now warned the Zaragoza rebels to surrender immediately, or they will be bombarded. The Barcelona military court began trying many prisoners today. Last night, a Spanish warship anchored near Gibraltar fired on rebel aircraft, which flew over the Rock to avoid the shells. Gibraltar was greatly shaken at the time, as shells exploded in the sky above the cinema and the air force headquarters. Another shell landed near the Rock Hotel, fortunately without injuring anyone. It is reported that government forces and rebels are currently engaged in fierce fighting in Seville, with government forces gradually approaching the city. (Reuters, 22nd)

Madrid: Many women in the capital have now formed teams, carrying handguns, and patrolling the streets day and night. All passing vehicles, including those owned by the People's Front parties' militias, are being inspected to prevent criminals from hiding. Furthermore, many insurgents now have whimsical ideas, hiding in various houses, opening fire from windows, and shooting at the militias in order to provoke them to retaliate, thereby wasting government bullets. The various organizations belonging to the People's Front have now ordered the militias not to retaliate against the insurgents unless they are sure of hitting them, in order to conserve bullets. (Havas, 22nd)

Spanish Prime Minister Announces Status of Suppression; Rebel Generals Dismissed

Madrid: Prime Minister 齊羅爾 recently gave an interview to this agency's correspondent, stating that the situation is increasingly favorable to the government. The city of Albacete in the southeast can be retaken by government troops this morning. The warships in the African Morocco area are scheduled to bombard the Moroccan capital of Tetouan today, demonstrating that the navy remains loyal to the government. Rebel leader General フランコ falsely imagines that the navy will turn against the government and should abandon this thought. As for フランコ himself, he is still in Melilla, Morocco. Finance Minister ラ摩斯 also stated that the government's current task is not only to suppress the rebels but also to provide food to the military and civilians. A troop of soldiers has just transported rice to the capital from the city of Valencia. He then detailed the government's combat plan, stating that government forces have advanced in three routes to retake the city of Albacete. The first troop set out from the city of Valencia and advanced southwest, now occupying the city of Almansa. The second and third troops set out from the cities of Murcia and Hellín, respectively, and advanced northwest. The city of Albacete will be captured soon. In addition, in the northern area, another troop set out from the city of Bilbao, advancing to capture the city of Burgos. Near the city of Huesca, the garrison mutinied, and the government has dispatched several airplanes to bomb them. A telephone call was recently made to postal workers in the city of Seville, learning that a general strike is underway there, and the airfield's fuel depot has been destroyed, which is detrimental to the rebels. (Havas, 23rd)

Madrid: The government gazette recently published two orders. The first appoints the Speaker of the House of Representatives, the Minister of Agriculture, the Director of the Ministry of Agriculture, and the Secretary-General of the State Council to form a cabinet committee under the control of the Prime Minister of the State Council. All government offices in the districts of Valencia, Alicante, Castellón, Cuenca, Albacete, and Murcia are under the control of this committee. The committee has now been established and has notified the Ministry of the Interior that it will dispatch reinforcements to the areas occupied by the rebels in order to retake them as soon as possible. The committee also declared that the army, navy, air force, and police forces in the above-mentioned areas are unwavering in their loyalty to the government. The second order dismisses rebel leader General フランコ and other generals. The resignation of Army Director General 蒲羅薩 has been approved, and the vacancy will be filled by General 貝那爾. The Ministry of the Interior has just ordered that any merchants who take advantage of the turbulent situation to raise prices will be subject to imprisonment. (Havas, 22nd)

Madrid: Officials announced today that government forces have recaptured the cities of Toledo and Guadalajara and are now attacking the rebel's arc-shaped front north of the capital. The government air force bombed the military airfield in the León region, destroying eight rebel aircraft. Several thousand militiamen are heading northeast to attack the rebels in the Chaila Valley, while another government force is flanking them from Catalonia. (国民電, 22nd)

Gibraltar: Several Spanish government seaplanes flew to La Línea in the afternoon (毗接 Gibraltar Port) to bomb the rebels. The rebels also sent seaplanes to intercept, and both sides exchanged machine-gun fire, resulting in no casualties. (哈元斯電, 22nd)

Madrid: Regarding the situation today, the government forces have made significant progress. However, the final outcome is currently difficult to predict. The government has announced that the cities of Toledo, La Granja, Guadalavilla, Sumocéller, and Telmansa have been retaken by government forces. Among them, the city of Toledo was retaken after fierce fighting, and a large number of rebel officers were captured. The rebels in La Granja, Guadalavilla, and Sumocéller suffered heavy casualties and abandoned countless weapons. In addition, General ムラ, the commander-in-chief of the rebel forces in the north, divided his troops into three routes to advance south, and government forces also divided into three routes to intercept them. The first route has engaged in battle in the city of Villalba, the second route has also made contact 60 kilometers north of the capital in Falerpigrales, and the third route has not yet encountered the enemy. (Havas, 22nd)

Gibraltar Shaken; Britain Issues Warning: No Fighting Allowed Nearby

Gibraltar: The British Representative Governor of Gibraltar today warned the Spanish authorities that if rebel aircraft and government warships engage in combat near Gibraltar again, as they did yesterday, the fortifications on both sides will be shelled. He also protested against the Spanish aircraft flying over the fortress. According to an official announcement, a Spanish aircraft dropped bombs near the British destroyer HMS Widgeon near 鐵利攻役, although they did not hit the ship. Several shells exploded near the ship, and the Widgeon fired a warning shot, after which the aircraft disappeared. (Reuters, 23rd)

The U.S. to Station Ships in the Atlantic and Mediterranean, But No Landing of Marines Under the Guise of Protecting Nationals

(Washington) Although the United States recently announced its policy of concentrating its fleet in the Pacific, Secretary of State Hull predicted today that the United States may restore its pre-1928 policy, citing the instability in Europe as a reason, and station a squadron of warships in the Mediterranean and the eastern Atlantic. Hull said that although this issue has not been actively considered, the government is not ignoring the possibility of such a move. (国民電, 22nd)

(Washington) When Secretary of State Hull met with reporters today, he mentioned that due to the instability in Europe, the US government may be forced to redeploy a naval squadron to European waters. Hull stated that although consideration of this issue has not made substantial progress, the US government will not ignore the problems caused by the absence of warships stationed in Europe. Since the last two cruisers of the US European Fleet were withdrawn in 1929, no US warships have been stationed in European waters. Hull also mentioned that the dispatch of US warships to Spain was due to the increasingly serious revolutionary situation in that country. The warships were sent purely as a precaution, and this action was reported to President Luo in detail. When asked if US Marines would be deployed to protect the lives of American citizens in Spain, Hull replied that neither the USS Oklahoma nor the USS Sinex, which were ordered to sail to Spain yesterday, were carrying Marines. According to reports, the USS Oklahoma is a training ship and is currently docked in Cherbourg, France, and will soon sail to Spain. The new heavy cruiser USS Quincy is en route to Europe and is expected to arrive in Gibraltar on Friday. (Reuters, 22nd)

(Washington) Windelin, the third secretary of the US Embassy in Spain, notified the State Department today that street fighting had broken out in the 爪泰拉馬 region, and an American woman was injured. Therefore, the State Department believes that the situation in Spain has become even more critical and is preparing to evacuate American citizens even before the US warships arrive in Spain. The first step is to notify the American shipping company to reroute the USS Uxide, which is scheduled to arrive in Marseille on Thursday, to Barcelona to evacuate American citizens who wish to leave Spain for refuge. This morning, the President of the Catalan Autonomous Government declared to the American Consul in Barcelona that he could not guarantee the safety of foreigners in the city. Secretary Windelin believes that if the situation in the Spanish capital does not change, there will be no problems with the embassy. However, armed youths have been requisitioning automobiles in the city, and government authorities have no time to address the grievances of foreigners. (国民電, 23rd)

(Washington) The State Department has just received a report from the US Embassy in Spain stating that "criminals in the Spanish capital may break into private residences under the pretext of searching for rebels, inspecting them one by one, thereby endangering the lives of residents." The State Department will read this report to reporters and stated that the US government has no intention of deploying Marines to land in Spain to protect its citizens. (日哈瓦斯電, 22nd)

(Washington) The State Department has just received reports stating that several hotels in the Spanish capital where American citizens reside have been under rebel fire for the past two days, and there is also a shortage of food in the city. (哈瓦斯電, 22nd)

Anglo-Egyptian Military Treaty Formally Signed Today

Cairo: The military clauses in the Anglo-Egyptian treaty were initialed last night after seven hours of negotiations. The treaty, as currently agreed upon, will be submitted to the delegations today, and a plenary session will be convened tomorrow for formal signing by British Resident Commissioner in Egypt, Sir Lampson, and Egyptian Prime Minister Nahas. (Havas, 23rd)

Britain, France, and Belgium Meet in London to Prepare for a Five-Nation Conference; A New Western European Pact to Replace the Locarno Treaty; Date Tentatively Set for September, Attitudes of Italy and Germany Undecided

(London) The meeting of Britain, France, and Belgium officially opened at 10:30 this morning. Attending were British representatives Prime Minister Baldwin, Foreign Secretary Eden, and Lord Privy Seal Halifax; French representative Foreign Minister Daladier; and Belgian representatives Prime Minister Janson and Foreign Minister Spaak. French Prime Minister Blum departed from the Paris airfield at 10:00 this morning and arrived during the lunch break. Today's meeting is merely a formality, as the three countries have already reached an understanding. It is reported that the French originally favored turning the temporary defense measures agreed upon by Britain, France, and Belgium into a permanent agreement, pending Germany's expression of remorse for its entry into the Rhineland. However, they have recently changed their position and agreed with the British view that the above-mentioned actions may cause other countries to misunderstand it as a hostile alliance. For this reason, the main task of today's meeting is to draft a communiqué as preparation for convening a conference of all signatories of the Locarno Treaty, namely Britain, France, Belgium, Germany, and Italy. The five-nation conference may be held in September. (Reuters, 23rd)

(London) The Anglo-Franco-Belgian conference was held for the first time this morning at 10 Downing Street, the Prime Minister's residence, lasting two hours. It is reported that "good progress has been made." It is generally believed that the representatives of the three countries have reached a compromise in principle. At the opening of the meeting, Prime Minister Baldwin first delivered a speech, welcoming the French and Belgian delegations, and stating that this discussion is of a preliminary nature. Afterwards, a plenary conference of the five signatory countries of the Locarno Treaty will be convened so that Italy and Germany can participate. The date of the five-nation conference was then discussed. The French delegation advocated holding it in August, while the British delegation advocated holding it in October, so as not to conflict with the regular session of the League of Nations General Assembly in September. The purpose of the five-nation conference is to establish a new Western European security pact to replace the Locarno Treaty, and because of Germany's participation, it can be seen what kind of aspirations the country has for international cooperation, and the contents of the understanding recently reached between Germany and Italy can also be measured in the five-nation conference. At this point, the meeting was adjourned until 3:30 PM. (Havas, 23rd)

(London) The Anglo-Franco-Belgian talks are now scheduled to begin tomorrow morning. French Foreign Minister Daladier led his entourage and arrived here at 7:00 PM, and stayed at a hotel in the West End. The Belgian delegation is scheduled to arrive here tomorrow morning, while French Prime Minister Léon Blum will not be able to arrive until noon tomorrow. According to political figures, there are two main difficulties in the three-nation talks: one is the Rhineland issue, and the other is the future European conference. Regarding the first point, Germany is actively constructing fortifications in the Rhineland area, and France is concerned that these fortifications will be completed soon. Therefore, France advocates that Germany should temporarily suspend work to show a spirit of compromise, otherwise it is unwilling to negotiate with it. As for Britain, it believes that since neither Britain nor France intends to use force, it is better to negotiate openly and honestly with Germany. Regarding the second point, France is deeply afraid that the European conference may attempt to revise the peace treaties, causing the Little Entente and the Balkan Entente to feel uneasy, so it opposes the idea. As for Belgium, its Foreign Minister Spaak recently declared that Belgium's main concern is its own security and is unwilling to assume other burdens. Therefore, political figures believe that Belgium will also disagree with the plan for the European conference. (Havas, 22nd)

(Rome) After the representatives of Britain, France, and Belgium began their meeting in London today, political figures here believe that this is an expression of hostility towards Italy by those countries, and that Italy should still refuse to participate in various European issues. The newspapers state that Italian diplomacy is not passive, as can be seen from the agreement recently reached between Germany and Austria. The 共中使者報載 claims that "If Italy wants to participate in European issues, the necessary condition lies in the removal of the remnants of the sanctions policy." (Havas, 23rd)

Austria Grants Amnesty, 10,000 Regain Freedom

(Vienna) President Miklas recently issued an amnesty order, pardoning approximately 10,000 political prisoners. Those who participated in the Socialist Party uprising in February 1934 and the Nazi Party riots in July of the same year and were sentenced to less than ten years of imprisonment have been pardoned, but 224 people with more serious circumstances (including eleven members of the Socialist Party) have not been pardoned. Former Ambassador to Italy, 林德倫, is also among them, which is contrary to general expectations. In addition, Germany and Austria had previously banned the entry of certain newspapers. Now, except for the German Nazi Party's organ "People's Observer" newspaper, the Party Army's organ "Attack" newspaper, and the Austrian government's organ "Federal Mail" newspaper, the ban on other newspapers has been lifted. (Havas, 22nd)

(Berlin) The Nazi Party's organ, the People's Observer, recently published a message stating that the Austrian Nazi Party cadres yesterday issued an order to all party members to strictly abide by the German-Austrian agreement. Austrian figures here have expressed disagreement with what the newspaper reported, stating that since the establishment of the German-Austrian agreement, the Austrian Nazi Party has ceased to exist. (Havas, 23rd)

British and Italian Forces in Africa Withdraw

Cairo: The British military authorities in Egypt, due to Italy's increased deployment of defensive troops in its Libyan territory, had previously built barracks, increased garrison strength, and arranged defenses in the city of Marsa Matruh, near the Libyan border, in November of last year. Now that the Italian-Ethiopian war has ended and some of the Italian troops stationed in Libya have returned to their country, the situation has eased considerably compared to the past. Therefore, a portion of the British troops stationed in the Marsa Matruh military camp, 2,000 men, have recently returned here. According to semi-official sources, another 2,000 British soldiers will be withdrawn in early October and redeployed to Cairo and other locations. (Havas, 22nd)

Eighteen Korean Communists Sentenced to Death

Seoul: Eighteen members of the Korean Communist Party, whose death sentences were approved by the Court of Appeals on June 16th, were executed at the prison execution grounds here today. (Reuters, 23rd)

Where is the Hirota Cabinet Going? (5)

— Jia He

If we regard Koki Hirota's fall from grace and the temporary withdrawal of the military's aggressive stance as a temporary ebb of rapid fascism, then it would seem that the power of political parties and the power of true democracy would grow proportionally. However, the reality is not so. Today's Japanese political parties, due to their own corruption and long-standing scandals of collusion with the zaibatsu (financial cliques), find it difficult to restore their own reputation. The established power of the military cannot be manipulated by unpopular political party leaders. Moreover, the elder statesmen and senior officials above the political parties do not have the courage to trust the political parties. Even the zaibatsu, after the "February 26th Incident," on the one hand, adopted deceptive tactics to eliminate public resentment, and on the other hand, abandoned their past policy of utilizing political parties and directly established relationships with military leaders. They each used the power of money to win over the military forces that could fight for their own interests, hoping to recoup significant returns in the future. Therefore, the political parties, having lost the vigorous support of the zaibatsu, speak of revitalization, but in fact, their heart is weakening day by day. Although, in the parliament, political parties still serve as a tool for passing bills, this is merely a dying ember's reflection. Currently, they are like a candle in the wind; as soon as the wind rises, even the bean-sized light will disappear. Moreover, outside of them, there are the bureaucratic forces that constantly deprive them of their interests. Hirota, in such an environment, plays the role of a shrewd and artful charmer. For the sake of the "Constitutional Politics" signboard, he woos the political parties to increase his power against the military; to restrain the political parties, he sometimes feigns the authority of the military. He veers with the wind, without fixed opinions. His reason for doing so is due to objective factors! Japanese capitalism, which has already entered the stage of oligarchical zaibatsu control over various industrial departments, has long rendered any political party that truly fights for democracy almost extinct. The current political parties, whether it is the Minseitō (Democratic Constitutional Party), the Seiyūkai (Association of Friends of Constitutional Government), the Shōwakai (Showa Society), or the Kokumin Dōmei (National League), although there are subtle differences in their political programs, all wear the mask of constitutionalism and mercilessly oppress the proletariat. Because the power of the proletariat is not yet enough to fluster the ruling class, they also utilize the parliamentary politics that are nominally run by political parties as a mechanism for dividing interests among themselves, as a regulator to restrain the frantic expansion of the military, and as a tool for formulating various laws and regulations to legally bind workers and peasants. If one day, the ruling class of Japan proves that this mechanism, this regulator, this tool, has lost its function, they will seize the ghost of Shirō Nonaka and others, in other words: they will adopt a rapid fascist path.

The Hirota cabinet is also like a scale, placing the forces of the political parties, the military, and the bureaucracy on it, and using specially made weights to measure them. During the extraordinary session of the Diet, he mobilized the political parties and admonished the military, while at the same time, he flattered the military and elevated their power, as evidenced by the May 18th ordinances of appointing active-duty lieutenant generals and major generals as military ministers and deciding officials. Some people believe, based on the historical development of this official system, that it is an indicator of the rise and fall of the power of political parties and the military, which is a fully justified reason. However, to conclude from this that the Hirota cabinet has lost its transitional nature and is a manifestation of yielding to the military would be too arbitrary. We know that the reform of the military system began in the second year of the Taisho era. At that time, liberalism was prevalent, and the Yamamoto cabinet, in view of the previous incident where the Terauchi cabinet was "poisoned" by Minister of the Army Uehara, disregarded the opposition of General Yoshimichi Hasegawa and the resignation of Minister of the Army Kigoshi, and expanded the qualifications of the Minister of the Army to include reservists. However, from the date of the promulgation of the official system to the establishment of the Hirota cabinet, there was no instance of a reserve lieutenant general or major general serving as Minister of the Army, but instead, the army interior was reduced to a tripartite political system – that is, the bad example of the heads of the three bureaus deciding personnel matters. Now, Hirota is reversing what the Yamamoto cabinet did, and he also has his reasons: first, the facts are such; second, it is better to let the Minister of the Army control the actual power than to let the three bureau chiefs decide personnel matters; third, Araki, Masaki, and others have already been incorporated into the reserve and will no longer be able to wield military power. From this perspective, Hirota's actions are definitely not without significance. Moreover, a mere ordinance regarding the active-duty military officer system is not enough to prove that the Hirota cabinet has lost its transitional nature.

Japan's Three Ministers' Conference Declaration. Ministry of Foreign Affairs Has Not Received Telegrammed Report.

Awaiting the Full Text Before Further Study.

(Nanjing) After the conference of the Japanese Ministers of Foreign Affairs, the Army, and the Navy on the 22nd, a semi-official declaration was issued, stating that if the Chinese government ignores Japan's special position, then Japan's North China policy will inevitably become more assertive. The implications of this declaration are significant. The reporter has inquired with relevant parties and learned that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has not yet received the full text of the declaration, nor has the embassy in Japan sent a telegrammed report. It is heard that our side will conduct a detailed study after receiving the full text of the declaration. (Central News Agency telegram, 23rd)

(Nanjing) Reuters reports that three Japanese cabinet members, Terauchi, and Nagano, issued a semi-official declaration on China, hoping that the special position of the Japanese government will not be ignored. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has not yet received the declaration, nor has the embassy in Japan reported it to the capital. Therefore, we have not yet understood its meaning. Whether it is necessary to make an appropriate response is still under study. (Special telegram, 23rd)

U.S. Republican Presidential Candidate's Speech

Advocates Liberalism, Promotes Peace with Justice.

Topeka, Kansas. Republican presidential candidate Landon stood before the Kansas State Capitol today and delivered a speech to thousands of supporters, expressing his acceptance of the party's nomination. This is the first sound of the Republican Party's participation in the presidential election campaign. In his speech, Landon promised to fully liberate the spirit of innovation and freedom in American enterprises so that the scope of commerce and professions can be expanded. He also vehemently criticized the current government's "New Deal" as inappropriate, saying that the slow recovery of prosperity is due to this. He also said that the country must avoid the influence of arbitrary and unstable monetary policies. The Republican Party advocates for thrift in government spending, but those in need must be assisted. He also proposed giving cash benefits to farmers to protect them from the effects of price fluctuations and to maintain their standard of living. As for diplomacy, it will be based on justice and will promote peace at all times. Furthermore, he will absolutely not participate in any plans that would involve the country in irrelevant wars or build false peace on military blocs. Finally, he guaranteed the restoration and maintenance of a free competition system. (Reuters telegram, 22nd)

Pan-American Peace Conference

Many Issues to be Discussed

(Washington) All countries in North and South America, except Canada, have been invited to participate in the Pan-American Peace Conference initiated by President Roosevelt. It is learned today that the conference will be lengthy. The Associated Press obtained the final draft of the conference agenda, which includes many issues, such as forming a "League of American Nations" through peaceful means, as well as other legal and economic issues. According to President Roosevelt's initial intention, there were not so many issues. Diplomats from Latin America feared that the Eighth Pan-American Conference, to be held in Peru's capital in 1938, would be greatly affected. The Associated Press learned that the agenda was expanded because diplomatic circles believed that some countries might express dissatisfaction if their proposals were not included in the agenda. (National News Agency telegram, 22nd)

British Soldier Shot Dead in Jerusalem

Four Others Wounded

Jerusalem. Holmes, a soldier of the 2nd Battalion of the Lancashire Fusiliers, was shot dead by an Arab sniper near Dur-Garmin today. Four other soldiers from the same battalion were also wounded, two of them seriously. (Reuters telegram, 22nd)

French Foreign Ministry Typist Sentenced to Two Years for Espionage for Germany

(Paris) Madame Claire Keller, a typist at the French Foreign Ministry for thirty years, was accused of passing on important information to German spies. After a secret trial by the court today, she was sentenced to two years in prison. Her husband, Mr. Keller, was also sentenced to two years in prison. A doctor named Barr, said to be the mastermind of the case, was sentenced to four years in prison. (Reuters telegram, 22nd)

Non-Stop Flight of Ten Thousand Li from Moscow to Khabarovsk Completed. A Feat by Soviet Russian Aviators.

(Moscow) According to a report from the Central Aviation Department of the People's Heavy Industry Committee, the ANT-25 aircraft, previously ordered by the department to make a 10,000-kilometer non-stop flight from Moscow to Chita, has now gloriously completed its mission. The aircraft was in the air for 56 hours and 20 minutes. The journey was fraught with difficulties. In the Zeya region, the aircraft suddenly encountered an Arctic cyclone and dense dark clouds. The aircraft stayed at an altitude of 4,000 meters for five hours, encountering headwinds with a speed of 70 kilometers per hour, and could only fly blindly. The aircraft was also covered with ice. When the aircraft passed over the Stanovoy Range, the entire crew struggled to overcome the conditions. When the aircraft crossed the Sea of Okhotsk, it encountered a southern cyclone and heavy fog. At this time, the entire aircraft was covered in ice. After receiving this report, the department considered that the aircraft had completed its mission and telegraphed an order to land. At 13:45 today (the 23rd), the aircraft safely landed on a small island near Chita in heavy fog, having traveled a total of 9,374 kilometers. It is reported that although the aircraft experienced many hardships, the pilot and crew are still in good condition. (TASS telegram, 23rd)

Typhoon Hits Japan. Lands on the Southeastern Coast.

Nagasaki. The typhoon that had been threatening China for several days turned towards Japan yesterday and landed on the southeastern coast of Japan at night. Details are not yet known due to traffic disruptions. Telegraph lines between Nagasaki and Kobe, Osaka, Tokyo, and Yokohama have been damaged. (Reuters telegram, 23rd)

Nagasaki. In the Nagasaki area, due to a strong storm that began in the evening of the 22nd, power was cut off, and the city became a dark world. Streetcars stopped, and traffic in the city was disrupted. Only the Sasebo line is still open for telegraphs. All lines to Tokyo, Osaka, Fukuoka, and Shimonoseki are closed. There has been considerable damage in various places, especially at sea. More than twenty motorized fishing boats have been shipwrecked, and more than thirty people are missing. Rescue efforts are currently underway. (Domei News Agency telegram, 23rd)

Moji. Since last night, a strong wind has struck the Kanmon area, with gusts reaching 40 meters per second, coupled with heavy rain. The Kanmon area has suffered severe damage. Since last night, all ships and civilian boats have taken refuge in the harbor, causing great congestion. Also, railways such as the Kagoshima Main Line and other lines have been disrupted due to landslides and flash floods. Train schedules are all delayed. Also, telegraph lines from Moji to Oita, Beppu, and Kagoshima are all closed. Many residential chimneys have collapsed in Moji city, causing great damage. (Domei News Agency telegram, 23rd)

(Tokyo) The Navy Ministry announced at 2:00 p.m. on the 23rd that the Combined Fleet, which was training in the Terashima Channel south of the Sasebo naval port, was hit by a typhoon with a maximum wind speed of 46 meters per second at dawn on the 23rd. Although countermeasures were taken, the auxiliary vessel Mamiya and the submarine I-50 were pushed to the coast by the wind. Rescue work is currently underway. The damage to the auxiliary vessel is minor, and the damage to the submarine is slightly greater. One member of the submarine crew suffered minor injuries. Three members of the Combined Fleet also suffered serious injuries due to the typhoon. (Domei News Agency telegram, 23rd)

Fukuoka. The Fukuoka Prefecture area has also suffered heavy damage due to the strong winds and rain since the night of the 22nd. More than a dozen people have been killed or injured, and a large number of houses have collapsed and bridges have been washed away, causing severe damage. (Domei News Agency telegram, 23rd)

In the 16th year, he was ordered to participate in the Northern Expedition and fought in the Hebei and Chahar regions, leading his troops as a vanguard and achieving remarkable feats. In recent times, he led his troops to suppress bandits and fought in Jiangxi and Shanxi, making significant contributions. It is deeply regrettable to hear that he was assassinated and killed. Li Shengda is posthumously awarded the rank of General of the Army and granted 5,000 yuan for funeral expenses, and the Executive Yuan is instructed to provide generous compensation. His life's achievements are to be recorded and placed in the National History Museum to demonstrate the government's respect and remembrance of his meritorious service. This order is issued.

Educational Broadcasting Special Issue

Secondary School Education (Part 2)

— Liao Shi-chieh, Professor, Kwong Hua University, Shanghai

The purpose of secondary school education, like the educational goals of a nation, shifts with the times. The educational goals set during the late Qing dynasty emphasized loyalty to the emperor, honoring Confucius, valuing public service, practicality, and martial spirit. By the late Guangxu and early Xuantong years, there was a gradual shift towards pragmatism, adopting a system of dividing subjects into arts and sciences. During the early years of the Republic, the educational goal was "to perfect morality through aesthetics." By the sixth year of the Republic, vocational education was emphasized. After the eighth year of the Republic, secondary schools adopted an elective system, striving to adapt to individual aptitudes. The new school system to be implemented in the eleventh year of the Republic stipulated six principles (these principles were revised by the First National Education Conference): (1) Based on the actual conditions of the country, (2) Adapting to the needs of the people's livelihood, (3) Increasing educational efficiency, (4) Promoting the development of individuality, (5) Making education easier to popularize, (6) Allowing for local flexibility. Since the National Revolutionary Army pacified the country and established the National Government, all facilities have taken on a new look, giving rise to the Three Principles of the People education. In April of the eighteenth year, the National Government promulgated an educational purpose: "The education of the Republic of China is based on the Three Principles of the People, with the purpose of enriching the people's lives, supporting the survival of society, developing the national economy, and continuing the life of the nation, striving for national independence, universal civil rights, and the development of the people's livelihood, in order to promote world harmony." The objectives of secondary school education were specifically stated in the General Outline of Secondary School Regulations promulgated by the Ministry in the twenty-second year: (1) Forging strong physiques, (2) Cultivating civic morality, (3) Nurturing national culture, (4) Enriching life skills and knowledge, (5) Cultivating a scientific foundation, (6) Forming labor habits, (7) Inspiring artistic interests. Since the Mukden Incident, the national crisis has been more serious than ever before, and the call for national defense education, production education, and education for extraordinary times has permeated the country. The recently released draft constitution of the Republic of China stipulates that the purpose of education is to promote the national spirit, cultivate national morality, train self-government capabilities, and enhance production knowledge and skills, in order to create healthy citizens. If we can grasp these four key points in the future and implement them effectively, we will surely achieve clear results and achieve the goal of saving the nation.

The curriculum of secondary schools is an interpretation of "national experience," indicating that many things must be experienced in childhood. Therefore, the curriculum of an era represents the needs of that era. The curriculum of secondary schools in our country has changed several times. The secondary school curriculum during the Guangxu era of the late Qing dynasty was divided into twelve subjects: (1) Self-cultivation, (2) Reading and lecturing on the classics, (3) Chinese literature, (4) Foreign languages, (5) History, (6) Geography, (7) Mathematics, (8) Natural history, (9) Physics and chemistry, (10) Law and finance, (11) Drawing, (12) Physical education. There were thirty-six hours per week. During the Xuantong era, secondary schools had a system of dividing subjects into arts and sciences. In the early years of the Republic, secondary schools abolished the reading of classics and added art subjects. The weekly teaching time was also reduced to thirty-four hours. In the eighth year, the Ministry of Education approved secondary schools to "consider local conditions and appropriately increase or decrease subjects and time." Schools adopted the elective system based on this document. After the implementation of the new system, the National Education Federation drafted a new curriculum standard outline. In the autumn of the eighteenth year, the Ministry of Education promulgated interim standards for primary and secondary school curricula, with significant changes in the course of study. In November of the twenty-first year, the Ministry of Education promulgated new standards for senior and junior high school curricula, with the following changes: (1) Party ideology teaching materials were incorporated into civics, history, geography, and other subjects, without setting up separate courses; (2) Elective subjects and the credit system were abolished; (3) The division of senior and junior high school students into arts and sciences was abolished; (4) Teaching hours were increased. After the promulgation of the new standards, schools in various places felt that the workload was too heavy, leaving no time for extracurricular activities. Therefore, the curriculum standards were revised by the Ministry of Education again in February of this year, with several key points:

(1) Emphasizing the development of students' ability to study independently and reducing their course burden. In recent years, people in society have commented that the secondary school curriculum emphasizes textbook knowledge, with too many total hours, too much teaching material, and a lack of independent study and interest, which may even hinder their physical and mental development. This revision of the subject and time schedule by the Ministry of Education first focuses on reducing the burden on students' courses and developing their ability to study independently. The total number of teaching hours per week before junior high school is 34-35 hours, now reduced to 31 hours; before senior high school is 31-34 hours, now changed to about 29 hours. The content of teaching materials for subjects with reduced hours is also reduced accordingly.

(2) Emphasizing national consciousness. After the Ministry of Education announced the revised subject and hour schedule for junior and senior high school mathematics, the second step was to revise and enrich the curriculum standards for junior and senior high school subjects, adding teaching materials on the national spirit to civics, Chinese language, history, and geography.

(3) Considering the individuality of students. The old senior high school subject and hour schedule lacked flexibility and did not fully consider the individuality of students. In this revision, the Ministry of Education stipulates that from the second academic year of senior high school, students can be divided into Group A and Group B. Students with an aptitude for natural sciences should study more mathematics; students with an aptitude for arts, history, and social sciences should study less mathematics and more Chinese, logic, and English to replace it.

(4) Taking into account students who do not go on to higher education. Senior high school is designed for students who go on to higher education, but in reality, many students do not go on to higher education. Under the current school system, these students should enter secondary vocational schools as the proper path. However, in fact, students' choice of schools is often not entirely rational, and the number of vocational schools is still insufficient. Therefore, the Ministry of Education stipulates in the revised senior high school subject and hour schedule that senior high schools may, depending on local conditions, offer simple vocational subjects (such as commerce, accounting, bookkeeping, statistics, applied writing, typing, agronomy, horticulture, cooperative societies, etc.) as elective subjects in the final academic year, so that those who cannot go on to higher education can still prepare for employment. In addition, the Ministry of Education is currently working on compiling editing outlines for each subject to facilitate teaching.

Teaching in secondary schools. The purpose of teaching is to enable students to learn. To enable students to learn, we must encourage students, guide students, and put students in a learning environment. Teachers and students often have many misunderstandings about learning:

First, misunderstanding learning materials as the results of learning. The most common misunderstanding is to focus on memorizing facts, repeating teaching materials, and doing prescribed exercises. These are not real learning. Everyone has forgotten the real results. Everyone pursues false learning, resulting in people who only know how to study from books and have no effect on dealing with people and things. This kind of education can only be called paper education or bookworm education.

When we say these things, we are not saying that concepts, facts, and experiences do not occupy an important position. We need these facts and we need memory-style tests. But we must always recognize that memorizing these facts is not the ultimate goal, but a method of obtaining learning results. If we tend to preserve facts or remember what teachers say, we will inevitably overemphasize memory, ignore application, and acknowledge doing homework as real learning. Reflective thinking and adaptability will not be obtained.

Second, misunderstanding grades as a representation of academic performance. When students see that remembering more facts can get high grades, their minds turn to grades. As long as they get grades, they are willing to use any method—rote memorization, plagiarism, cheating. As a result, they fall to a lower level and cannot even achieve the point of doing homework. Not only have they not developed good behavior, but even bad attitudes have become deeply ingrained. And after setting a passing grade, students only seek to get by and are unwilling to study with all their heart and mind. Spiritual training is simply out of the question.

But some people also say that students with excellent grades in school seem to have a greater chance of success in society. Can grades represent performance? To answer this question, we must distinguish between different situations. If the student's purpose is to pursue grades and not to obtain real understanding and ability, then his grades may not represent performance. If the student's purpose is not grades, but he gets high grades because he has sustained attention, unremitting effort, keen discernment, and the ability to search and explore, then his grades can represent his attainments.

Grading is also very difficult. Real learning must obtain new responses and be applied in real situations. Repeating teaching materials does not necessarily indicate understanding. Only by creating a new realm can we test understanding and ability. To put it more thoroughly, only the practical problems that arise in life can test the results of learning.

Page 10

Japanese Warships Conduct Large-Scale Maneuvers in the Waters off Fujian and Taiwan

More than 70 warships and 50,000 soldiers and sailors will conduct exercises for one week starting July 25th.

Fuzhou dispatch. After Japan decided to actively develop political and economic power in Fujian and Guangdong provinces, it increased the authority of the Governor-General of Taiwan, ordering him to command the consuls stationed in Fujian and Guangdong provinces. The Governor-General's Office of Taiwan convened a meeting of consuls stationed in Fujian and Guangdong provinces a month ago to discuss implementation plans and designated Magong as a naval base, prohibiting Chinese merchant ships from entering and exiting, and Keelung as an air force base, where a large airfield is currently under construction. Recently, fleets have been dispatched repeatedly from Taiwan, intruding into the territorial waters and inner harbors of our country's Fujian and Guangdong provinces for patrols. Moreover, strange airplanes have appeared from time to time along the coasts of eastern and southern Fujian, spying on strategic locations or taking pictures, with malicious intentions. Recently, Li Shijia, the commander of the Fuzhou naval port, and Lin Guogeng, the commander of the Xiamen naval port, jointly telegraphed the Ministry of the Navy, requesting that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs be consulted to inform the Japanese ambassador that if Japanese warships enter our country's harbors in the future, they should notify our local naval authorities in advance for reception, and should not enter and exit arbitrarily, as this would hinder coastal defense and disturb the people's minds. A large Japanese fleet, consisting of more than 70 warships and approximately 50,000 soldiers and sailors, is scheduled to conduct cross-sectional maneuvers in the waters bordering Taiwan and Fujian for one week starting on July 25th. The Japanese consul in Fujian requested that our country send personnel to observe the maneuvers. The provincial government replied yesterday, requesting that they not disturb coastal fishing boats and island residents during the maneuvers. It is also reported that after the large-scale Japanese naval maneuvers, preparations will be made for a full-scale air defense exercise on Taiwan Island. The Governor-General's Office of Taiwan has suspended logging on the entire island for ten years for the sake of arranging air defense, and will purchase wood for use from Fujian, having sent Gangtian Shang to Fujian to negotiate purchasing and transporting methods. In addition, recently, foreign monks have been discovered in various coastal areas, sneaking into various villages to investigate local conditions and troop deployments, or carrying cameras to secretly photograph strategic areas, which are suspected of espionage. The provincial government has repeatedly received reports from various parties and has ordered the governments of all counties to quickly check household registrations, and to detain and strictly interrogate anyone with an unclear origin, and to send personnel to secretly investigate to prevent unscrupulous elements from operating and undermining national defense. In addition, Taiwanese people are engaged in various illegal businesses in Fujian, such as opium dens, gambling dens, private pawnshops, and other illegal businesses. Although our government has repeatedly lodged protests and the Japanese consul has promised to ban them, it has not yet been implemented. (July 22nd)

Serious Incident Occurs in Tianjin: Company Commander of the Municipal Government Guard Detained by Japanese Police Station; Special Agent Killed by Gunfire Due to Misunderstanding

Tianjin dispatch. At 0:30 PM on the 22nd, a serious incident involving foreign relations occurred near the Jin'gang Bridge in Hebei, Tianjin. The details are as follows:

Zhou Fengling, the company commander of the 7th Company of the Tianjin Municipal Government Guard Battalion, went to the Zhongyuan Company in the Japanese Concession in casual clothes on the evening of the 21st. A special agent from the Japanese Concession Police Station saw him and thought he looked suspicious. He searched Zhou's body, and although nothing was found, Zhou was still considered to be a bandit and taken to the Japanese Police Station, where he was brutally tortured and interrogated, ordered to confess the whereabouts of his accomplices and what cases he had committed. Zhou, under duress, dared not admit that he was a company commander of the Municipal Government Guard Battalion, but only confessed that he was a tea server at the Xiaoying Company at the Beining New Railway Station. At noon on the 22nd, the Japanese Police Station did not notify the Tianjin Public Security Bureau, and immediately sent Special Agent Candidate Patrol Chief Zhang Delu and Special Agent Zhang Xuanzhi to escort Zhou in Japanese Police Station car No. 963, driven by driver Chen Changtai, directly to the Hebei New Railway Station to verify Zhou's confession. At 0:30 PM, they arrived in front of the Municipal Government near the Jin'gang Bridge. Zhou struggled desperately, hoping that the guards in front of the Municipal Government would discover him and report to the mayor for rescue. Zhang Delu, who was escorting Zhou, immediately struck Zhou's lower body with a police baton. Zhou was beaten and shouted for help. The guards inside the Municipal Government heard the sound and came out to see. At that time, car No. 963 could not move forward and stopped on the side of the road. The guards saw that the person in the car was their company commander, and the two special agents were extremely fierce and humiliating him. In a moment of public outrage, without even asking the details, they tried to rescue Zhou. Zhang Delu, who had been torturing Zhou, fearing that Zhou would escape, pulled out his gun and fired a warning shot at Zhou's head. The guards became even more outraged and retaliated in the chaos. Zhang Delu was shot four times in the head and died instantly in the car. Zhang Xuanzhi jumped out of the car and fled to the nearby Dahua Dye Shop. Driver Chen Changtai, in a panic, ran to the Jintang River, intending to jump into the water to avoid bullets, but was stopped by a police officer on duty at the Jin'gang Bridge. After the incident, Zhou knew that his crime was too great and went to the Municipal Government to report. Car No. 963 and driver Chen Changtai were both taken to the Municipal Government. At that time, the Municipal Government was closing up after hours and no one was in charge. After reporting to Mayor Zhang Zizhong and Secretary-General Ma Yanchong, they rushed to the Municipal Government one after another and immediately summoned Zhou Fengling to investigate the truth. At this time, Zhang Xuanzhi had reported to the Japanese Police Station. Japanese Vice-Consul Nishida, Japanese Police Station Chief Wakui, Criminal Department Chief Owa, Judicial Section Chief Okayama, Police Department Chief Fujii, Japanese Army Headquarters Staff Officer Nakamura, and Military Police Branch Chief Ikegami all arrived at the scene of the incident to investigate. Many plainclothes special agents and police officers were also investigating and guarding the vicinity of the crime scene. For a time, traffic on Tian'an Road, South Road, and North Jin'gang Bridge was completely cut off, and there were thousands of onlookers. After the Japanese Police Station Military Police took photos, they entered the Municipal Government to visit Mayor Zhang Zizhong. Vice-Consul Nishida and Police Station Chief Wakui verbally protested, reserving their rights to investigate and demand in this case. The two sides talked for a long time, until three o'clock, when Nishida left. Wakui and Ikegami waited for the prosecutor from the District Procuratorate to complete the examination before returning to the station. At 5:30, the District Court sent Prosecutor Tu Zhang to examine the body. Afterwards, he filled out the death certificate, which was taken by the Japanese side. The body was then transported to the Japanese Concession Police Station and handed over to its family for burial. In the evening, car No. 963 and driver Chen Changtai were both released after being interrogated by the Municipal Government. In addition to urgently reporting the facts to Song Zheyuan, Zhang Zizhong also sent Councillors Chen Dongsheng and Lu Nansheng to visit Japanese Consul-General Tajiri, Chief of Staff of the Japanese Garrison Headquarters Nagami, Commander of the Military Police Headquarters Fujii, and Police Station Chief Wakui to explain that this case was under investigation and that if it was the fault of the company commander of the Guard Battalion, it would not be tolerated and would be dealt with severely. As of the evening of the 22nd, the Japanese side had not made any serious statements. In addition to detaining Zhou Fengling, the authorities were investigating the truth of the incident and were doing their best to eliminate the tense atmosphere in foreign relations, hoping that no more serious problems would arise as a result. According to Cheng Xixian, the director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, the incident was unfortunate, but the Japanese Police Station did not notify our side in advance, resulting in this misunderstanding, which is deeply regrettable. Zhang Delu's open firing in the Chinese territory was the main cause of this case. Therefore, in future negotiations, this point may be used as a tool to reduce the seriousness of the incident, which is also unknown. (July 22nd)

Smuggling in Southern Fujian Has Somewhat Subsided; Tax Inspectors Cooperate in Apprehending Along the Coast; Customs Revenue of Fuzhou and Xiamen Increases

Xiamen dispatch. The trend of smuggling in Fujian Province was rampant at one time between last winter and this spring. After the Third Pacification District cracked down on the smuggling agency Nanxin Foreign Firm in Shishi, the large-scale secret smuggling agency in Southern Fujian disintegrated. Subsequently, the Provincial Government established a Tax Inspection Office, setting up sixteen branch offices along the coast, and the trend gradually subsided with joint land and sea arrests. The Provincial Tax Inspection Office recently sent Zhen Yaogong and Wang Rulin to inspect smuggling affairs in Southern Fujian. They arrived in Xiamen on the 21st. According to Wang, "This trip passed through Quanzhou, Anhai, Zhangzhou, Shima, Zhangpu, Jiuzhen, Fotan, Yi'an, Meizhou, Yunxiao, and other places, and the results were very good. The trend of smuggling in various places has gradually subsided, and the customs revenue of Fuzhou and Xiamen has been increasing month by month. The most rampant smuggling in Southern Fujian is in Zhangpu and Jiuzhen. Since the establishment of inspection branch offices, smugglers have been repeatedly cracked down on, and all have been transferred to Chihu, Fotan, and Yunxiao for unloading via Meizhou. We are currently intercepting and arresting in this direction. The smuggling in Xiamen is that general smugglers transport imported smuggled goods to the interior. When reporting goods for transportation, they often report more than they actually have to the tax bureau, concealing and evading transportation. Today, we discussed with the Xiamen Finance Bureau that from now on, when merchants transfer goods to the interior and pay taxes, the tax forms must be investigated truthfully to see if they match, to prevent smuggling evasion. Xiamen is a small island, and smuggled imported goods must be transported to the interior to have a way out. If the Xiamen Tax Bureau and the inland inspection offices can strictly intercept their outlets, Xiamen smugglers will be no different from being sentenced to death. Currently, coastal anti-smuggling in Fujian Province is temporarily the responsibility of the Security Corps. The Inspection Office decided to organize a tax police regiment within one month, divided into three brigades, which will be distributed to various coastal areas to fight smuggling after its establishment," and so on. (July 23rd)

Harsh Examples of Restrictions on Chinese Workers in Taiwan

Chinese businessmen and general overseas Chinese all suffer cruel treatment.

Xiamen dispatch. The Taiwan authorities have recently increased the number of Chinese workers going to Taiwan, with a total of more than 7,000 people from January to June. Ten thousand Taiwanese people have lost their jobs as a result, so they blame it on the excessive number of Chinese workers entering the country and restrict their entry. Chinese workers go to Taiwan because they are recruited by Taiwan's military and mining industries. Now that they feel there is a surplus, they are adding restrictions. The restriction methods are: (1) A certificate to go to Taiwan must be guaranteed by a Taiwanese person or a local shop, and each person must pay four yen. This type of traveler is mostly a property owner or tourist, and the treatment is quite polite. (2) Ordinary businessmen who have a passport from our Ministry of Foreign Affairs must first obtain a passport from the local government, paying a fee of 4.6 yuan, and then ask the local Japanese consul to sign it, paying a visa fee of four yuan. (3) Laborers must go through import procedures handled by the Nangoku Company, which was established by the Japanese. It is located in ports that have direct shipping routes to Taiwan and was established 37 years ago. Laborers who go to Taiwan must first have photos taken and vaccinated at a photo studio and hospital designated by the company. Then, the company will issue a worker's passport. They must pay a handling fee and fare of ten yuan in Xiamen to obtain a worker's passport. After arriving in Taiwan, the passport must be carried with them at all times and cannot be separated from them for even a moment. Those who forget to bring it when they are inspected are fined 50 yuan. Moreover, Chinese workers in Taiwan can never change jobs and are treated like slaves. Even if they have some savings and want to abandon being a Chinese worker and go into business, they are not allowed. During their stay, they are constantly summoned by the Japanese police. If their answers are slightly hesitant, they will be immediately detained and sent back to Xiamen. Those who are deemed unsatisfactory by the Japanese police are also detained and sent back. Some of the Chinese workers who are sent back are penniless and become beggars. The restrictions on businessmen in Taiwan used to be relatively lenient, but recently, Taiwanese businessmen who have a passport from our Ministry of Foreign Affairs and have completed the formalities are often strictly inspected by the Japanese police and are required to carry 200-300 yuan in cash with them to be recognized as businessmen going to Taiwan. Otherwise, they will be considered workers, or those with a rough appearance will also be considered workers, and their passport from our Ministry of Foreign Affairs will be revoked, and they will have to pay another five yen to be issued a worker's passport, so they will not be able to change jobs in Taiwan for the rest of their lives. Although the Japanese police are strict with Chinese workers, they do not pay attention to their thinking and social activities because they are not intellectuals. Those who obtain worker's passports to avoid the attention of the Japanese police will be punished, detained, or sent back if they are found out. The Nangoku Company, which handles the import of Chinese workers, has recently been ordered by the Taiwan authorities to restrict Chinese workers from going to Taiwan, using the number of Chinese workers needed in Taiwan and the amount as the standard. In addition, those who have trachoma or other infectious diseases are also not allowed to go to Taiwan. The Taiwan authorities' reason for restricting Chinese workers and Chinese from entering the country is that the number of unemployed local Taiwanese people has increased sharply, which they blame on the excessive number of Chinese workers and Chinese entering the country. In fact, the unemployment of Taiwanese people is due to the Japanese implementing strict control in Taiwan. Most of the larger industrial and commercial businesses and raw material agriculture that Taiwanese people have always operated have been taken over by the Japanese and merged into large enterprises organized by the Japanese. After the merger, the number of employees used gives priority to hiring Japanese people, and the rationalization of large enterprises requires fewer personnel than individual operators, so the unemployment of Taiwanese people is increasing, not being seized by Chinese workers and Chinese. (July 23rd)

Anhui Provincial Government Moves Forward: Anhui-Guangdong Rice and Sugar Exchange Sales; Anhui Province Has Bumper Rice Harvest, New Goods Appear on the Market at Low Prices

Wuhu dispatch. Rice, a special agricultural product of Anhui Province, used to export 6-7 million shi annually from Wuhu port during its peak, with Guangdong being the largest sales market. However, since the invasion of foreign rice, the Guangdong market has been monopolized. In recent years, the value of rice shipped from Annam, Siam, and other foreign countries to Guangdong Province has exceeded 70 million yuan, and the amount of Anhui rice needed is only one-tenth or one-twelfth of what it used to be. The prosperity or decline of Anhui rice trade is related to the economic lifeline of Anhui Province, and this situation is no longer something that merchants can save. Guangdong's trade goods with Anhui were originally dominated by white sugar. In recent years, the province has worked hard to develop sugar production and has added five new-style sugar mills. The annual sugar production has increased to more than 60,000 tons. Now it is also seeking a way out to prevent oversupply. The Anhui Provincial Government intends to take this opportunity to try political means to revive the rice market, that is, to imitate the method of exchanging and promoting special products agreed by the Shanxi and Suiyuan provinces, and to mutually sell Anhui rice and Guangdong sugar. Guangdong sugar is suitable for the needs of Anhui Province, which is enough to achieve mutual benefit. It is currently being planned and will be realized in the near future. The finances of all industries in Anhui Province may have a turning point towards activity. This year's agricultural affairs in Anhui Province have been blessed with timely sunny and rainy weather, and even distribution of water and drought. Rice has already had a bumper harvest, and the new early rice has already appeared on the market. The entire autumn harvest is in sight, and the market price has fallen sharply. The opening price of the new market is only around 6.56 yuan. At the same time, the old rice stockpiled by various rice industries is being forced to open warehouses and sell urgently, so the rice price still has a downward trend. Under this environment, in addition to rushing to complete the construction of 48 county agricultural warehouses, which are under construction, to facilitate adjustment, it is also necessary to promote the exchange and sales of Anhui rice and Guangdong sugar as soon as possible. (July 22nd)

Transfer of Jurisdiction for Xu Wancheng

Xu Wancheng, an editor at the Shanghai Longwen Bookstore, previously published a periodical in Shanghai titled "Xu Wancheng's Work Report."
