Changshu

Melon Boat Robbed at Night

Watermelons are on the market in the hot summer. The produce from the area west of Mudu is considered the best, and there is fierce competition for sales in the city. Tang Xiaodi and others, residents outside the West Gate, pooled their money to become watermelon vendors. They took a boat to the countryside to buy watermelons. Unexpectedly, while sailing on the West Lake near Zhang's Tomb Bridge, it was already midnight when they were suddenly intercepted by a pirate ship. All the watermelons were robbed, and the clothing of everyone on board was also stripped away. Tang was wounded by the robbers for resisting. Because they had no money to buy more watermelons, they had to return with an empty boat. They have now reported the incident to the authorities for investigation.

Wuxi

Aftermath of the Silk Factory Strike

The Wuxi silk factory strike has been settled through the efforts of the Party and government, and a deep understanding has been reached between labor and management. Satisfactory results have been achieved on issues such as wage standards, working hours, bonuses, and holidays. Work resumed in full on the twenty-first. The Silk Factory Association also held a general membership meeting at 5:00 PM on the twenty-second to discuss in detail issues such as internal reorganization and wage regulations. Unexpectedly, a small number of family members of workers still in custody on suspicion of instigation, and other undesirable elements, felt that the settlement of the strike was detrimental to them. They spread various rumors, causing only twenty or thirty female workers to report to the Yongtai and Zhang Liangyuan Yongchang factories outside the South Gate that afternoon. Although calls for work were made again yesterday morning, the female workers still did not report to work. The two factories have reported the matter to the Party and government, as well as the General Labor Union, for handling.

Rectification of Grain Reserves in Various Counties

Zang Qifang, the Special Commissioner of the Second District Administrative Inspectorate, believes that the grain reserves in each county should be sufficient to meet the needs of the entire county population for six months. Each county, district, township, and town should establish a granary, and granaries should also be set up at suitable locations for separate storage. However, the regulations for grain requisition should apply equally to farmers and merchants, with no distinction. However, merchants may pay in cash instead of grain. Yesterday, he specifically ordered the counties under his jurisdiction to vigorously promote the expansion of existing charitable granaries. Counties where granaries have not yet been built may temporarily borrow public buildings or temples and civilian houses. The deadline for the completion of all county granaries is the end of December of this year.

Jiangyin

Sixty-Year-Old Man Murdered

Tong Degen, a resident of the 14th household of the 2nd Jia of the 2nd Bao of Zhongshan Town (Wenheng Bridge Hongjian Street) in the city, currently delivers newspapers for the Liuhe Telegraph Office. His wife, Sanmei, has been engaging in immoral behavior. A man from Zhenjiang named Zhang Goulang, sixty-two years old, who used to run a dim sum shop in Kunshan, came to Jiangyin to visit his uncle, Zhang Aliu. Three days ago, Tong Sanmei, seeing his pitiful state, invited him to stay at their home. Last night (the 21st), he was suddenly murdered with a kitchen knife. It was not discovered until dawn on the 22nd. The incident was reported to the Public Security Bureau, which in turn reported it to the county. Investigator Shen Cheng went to examine the body. The throat was cut, severing the three tubes. The murderer is unknown, and the cause of death is unclear. The landlady, Tong Sanmei, and neighbors such as Gu Ruyang were taken to the county for questioning.

Bengbu

Two Major Bandits Hiding the Ransom Victim Captured

Zhou Zhixiu, Fan Guiying, Sun Guilan and other major bandits who roamed northern Anhui, gathered a crowd of bandits some months ago and kidnapped the farmer Bai Zhenfang and his son Bai Xianrui in the Baijia Lake area of Huaiyuan County. Subsequently, the Bai family reported the case to the Huaiyuan County Government and requested their arrest. The county government dispatched teams to search and arrest them in different directions. The bandits Zhou and Fan, seeing that the government's arrest was imminent, secretly took Bai Xianrui to Bengbu and hid him in a recruitment office of a certain division on Zhongzheng Street, in order to extort a ransom nearby. This was discovered by the Huaiyuan County Government, which dispatched county police and militia on the morning of the twenty-first at 7:00 AM, together with the staff of the Second District Office, to surround the bandit den according to the address. Unexpectedly, the bandits opened fire to resist arrest, wounding a county policeman. The police and militia also returned fire. Ultimately, the bandits were outnumbered and overwhelmed. Zhou Zhixiu was shot and fell to the ground on the spot, and Fan Guiying was also captured. Sun Guilan took the opportunity to escape. The ransom victim, Bai Xianrui, was also rescued. At 10:00 AM, the Huaiyuan County police and militia escorted the two bandits, Zhou and Fan, and the ransom victim onto a small steamer to be taken to the county. After the boat traveled three miles, Zhou, who was injured and untied, jumped into the river and committed suicide. When the boat stopped and searched for him, he had already drifted away without a trace.

(Front row, from left) Huang Guangrui, Liu Jiwen, Yu Hongjun, and Cai Jingjun (Photo by International News Agency)

Huang's Talk

According to a written statement released by Huang Guangrui on the ship, (Q) What was the cause of the Guangdong Air Force's secession from the Southwest, and what was the process at that time? (A) Air Force comrades have always adhered to the Premier's instruction to save the country through aviation. Everyone is of one mind. If it is not for the sake of the cause and for the sake of saving the people, we will never sacrifice ourselves. We especially oppose civil war. This Southwest openly advocates resistance against Japan, but the name and reality do not match. Moreover, it borrows military officers from a certain country to participate in the war, provoking internal strife, and the disaster is imminent. In order to preserve the local area, preserve the lifeline of the country, and preserve the glory of the group, we must make a clear statement to promote Commander-in-Chief Chen Bonan's awakening. We have never received any movement or assistance from anyone beforehand. It is purely the consensus of all officers and soldiers to unanimously support the central government, unify military power, and eliminate civil war from now on. Therefore, at dawn on July 18, I personally led the squadron leaders of all squadrons under my command to fly all sixty-five large and small warplanes in Guangdong to Shaoguan for concentration, waiting for orders to advance or retreat. At that time, all flight personnel enthusiastically obeyed orders and competed to be pilots. After the planes took off, the Guangdong military police were not aware of it. The other planes were led by squadron leaders Tan Shou, Tao Zuode, Xie Mang, Ao Yuanqing, Ma Tinghuai, He Jingwei, Guo Hanting, Deng Xiangan, and deputy squadron leader Yu Binwei, and others, and flew to Shaoguan. I, along with Chief of Staff Chen Zhuolin, Principal Hu Hanxian, and Director Wu Jianwen, and others, flew four planes to Hong Kong. Soon after, hundreds of unarmed pilots, mechanics, and other staff members successively went to Hong Kong for concentration, breaking away from the Southwest relationship. Currently, a part of my troops is stationed in Shaoguan, and a part is stationed in Nanchang. They will be transferred back to Guangdong in the coming days for centralized waiting for orders. (Q) What is the mission of this trip and the schedule for the round trip? (A) To meet with Chairman Lin, Chairman Chiang, and other senior officials to express the sincerity of the Guangdong Air Force officers and soldiers in supporting the central government, and to report on the past work and request instructions on the future training strategy. I will also go to Nanchang to comfort my troops. I will first go to Beijing and then go to Nanchang, Ji'an, or Shaoguan, or return to Guangdong via Shanghai for further instructions.

Import of Foreign Cotton Seeds Only Allowed Through Shanghai to Facilitate Inspection and Disinfection, Effective August 1 This Year

The Ministry of Industry previously approved the National Economic Commission's Cotton Industry Control Committee's request that, before the plant and insect pest inspections are universally implemented in various inspection bureaus, the import of foreign cotton seeds should only be allowed through Shanghai in order to facilitate inspection and disinfection. After the Ministry of Industry consulted the Ministry of Finance for review, it also ordered the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau to comply. It is now learned that the Ministry of Industry has approved the Ministry of Finance's consultation, according to the report submitted by the Inspector General of Customs, that it will be implemented from August 1 this year. In addition to requesting the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to notify the governments of various countries to inform their exporting merchants, the Shanghai Inspection Bureau was also ordered to inform them. After receiving the order, the bureau has dispatched personnel to contact the Jianghai Customs Commissioner to coordinate the procedures.

Representatives of Chambers of Commerce from Various Provinces, Cities, and Counties Petition in Beijing Last Night, Requesting Amendments to the Chamber of Commerce Law and Trade Association Law, Implementing Income Tax After First Eliminating Disguised Likin Taxes, and Revising Article 681 of the Civil Code and Partnership Liabilities

Representatives from chambers of commerce of twenty-one provinces, cities, and counties, acting upon the resolution of the joint conference, led by the presidium members Wang Xiaolai, Yu Rongqiao, Yuan Duanfu, Yu Xiaochuan, and Cai Chang, departed from the Shanghai North Station yesterday, taking the Shanghai-Beijing through train at 4 PM and the Beijing-Shanghai overnight express train at 11 PM to petition in Beijing. After arriving in Beijing this morning, they will gather at the Nanjing Chamber of Commerce at 9 AM to submit petitions to the Central Party Headquarters, the Executive Yuan, the Legislative Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, and the Ministry of Industry, requesting the elimination of disguised likin taxes before implementing income tax, and the amendment of the Chamber of Commerce Law, the Trade Association Law, and commercial laws regarding partnership liabilities. The original text of the three petitions is recorded below:

Petition One: Regarding the matter of submitting a petition, the affiliated associations, in order to assist in smuggling suppression, address tax system issues, and revise commercial laws, convened a joint conference in Shanghai on the 20th of this month at the invitation of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce. The discussion of various cases concluded on the 22nd of this month. Regarding smuggling suppression, it is proposed to establish a National Smuggling Suppression Association in Shanghai to supervise local industries and businesses, strictly investigate whether there are privately imported and tax-evading goods, and conduct spot checks and register their inventories at any time. Regarding the tax system, (1) it is requested that the Ministry of Finance eliminate disguised likin taxes in various provinces by a set deadline, such as the production and sales tax in Hunan, the bandit suppression and reconstruction donation in Jiangxi, various special taxes in Guangdong, the landing tax in Sichuan, the silkworm silk improvement fee in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, and the special consumption tax in Shaanxi, Gansu, and Yunnan. (2) It is requested that the Ministry of Finance implement income tax only after all disguised likin taxes have been eliminated and foreign nationals can pay taxes uniformly according to regulations. Regarding commercial laws, they fall into three major categories: (1) Regarding the liability of partners for debts, it should follow the compromise method adopted by the Legislative Yuan in October of the 23rd year of the Republic. If a partner registers their name, address, and capital contribution with the government, they should be liable for sharing losses according to their capital contribution. The draft Commercial Registration Law proposed by the Legislative Yuan in October of that year should be promptly deliberated and passed. If the Commercial Registration Law is considered a procedural law and partnership debt is stipulated in Article 681 of the Debt Section of the Civil Code, and it is inconvenient to change the substantive law with procedural law, it is requested that the compromise method proposed in October of that year be added after Article 681 of the Civil Code for reference and to avoid obstacles. This principle has already been submitted to the Legislative Yuan. (2) In the Trade Association Law, the following articles should be amended as appropriate: (A) The provision that a trade association can only be organized if there are at least seven businesses in the same industry is too restrictive. When businesses in the same industry believe that it is necessary to organize a trade association, they should be allowed to apply for establishment without being subject to this restriction. (B) In addition to the articles of association, trade associations should formulate industry rules through the consensus of the industry to standardize prices, limit production, and set quality standards. These industry rules should be considered part of the articles of association, and those who violate them should be subject to penalties and confiscation of their goods in violation of the agreement. If necessary, they may appeal to the court for a judgment to be enforced. (C) If businesses in the same industry do not comply with the provisions of Article 7 of the Trade Association Law to join the association, the government may impose sanctions, or even order them to suspend their business. (3) In the Chamber of Commerce Law, the following articles should be amended as appropriate: (A) Clearly define the organizational system of commercial groups to maintain a close relationship between trade associations and chambers of commerce. (B) Chambers of commerce should have the right to express opinions when amending laws and regulations. (C) If a trade association does not join the chamber of commerce, or joins but does not fulfill its due obligations, the competent authority may reorganize or rectify the trade association or punish its officers. (D) The number of executive and supervisory committee members of the chamber of commerce should be appropriately increased. The above points have all been drafted into articles and submitted separately to the Legislative Yuan and the Ministry of Industry. The undersigned believes that your association has the responsibility to lead people's groups and preside over national administration. All of the above-mentioned resolutions should be presented to your association by the representatives attending this session, along with a petition, and respectfully request that your association be informed of everything and that you grant separate instructions for the public convenience. Respectfully submitted to the Central Executive Committee of the Kuomintang and the Executive Yuan.

Petition Two: Regarding the matter of submitting a petition, it is noted that the current Chamber of Commerce Law and Trade Association Law were deliberated, decided, and promulgated around the 18th year of the Republic, and more than seven years have passed since then. Recently, with the rapid invasion of the world economic tide and the unchecked smuggling in North China, the upper and lower levels of society unanimously feel that if the organizational strength of commercial groups is not strengthened so that they can lead the industry and command flexibly, the national economy will be on the verge of total collapse. The affiliated associations, in view of the importance of their responsibility, convened a joint conference in Shanghai at the invitation of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce. The issue discussed, in addition to assisting in the detection of smuggled goods, was the amendment of the Chamber of Commerce Law and the Trade Association Law as the main agenda item of this session. Now, the joint associations of provincial chambers of commerce of seven provinces and the chambers of commerce of fourteen cities and counties have drafted several articles for revising the Chamber of Commerce Law and the Trade Association Law, representing their humble opinions. The chambers of commerce attending this conference have each appointed one representative to present everything to your Yuan (Department). This document is prepared and submitted to request your review and adoption for implementation, for the sake of the public interest. In addition to submitting it separately to the Ministry of Industry (Legislative Yuan), respectfully submitted to the Legislative Yuan (Ministry of Industry).

Petition Three: Regarding the matter of submitting a petition, the affiliated associations, in order to assist in the issue of detecting smuggled goods, convened a joint conference in Shanghai at the invitation of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce. They deeply believe that the quality of the national tax system is closely related to the national economy and the people's livelihood. If the roots of bad taxes are not completely eradicated, the people's livelihood will be haggard, and even good taxes will have no hope of being implemented. As for good taxes, they also have their own conditions for implementation. Since the tax system imitates advanced countries in Europe and the United States, special phenomena that are unique to our country but not found in advanced countries should also be improved one by one to avoid bad results from good taxes. This is not an overstatement by the affiliated associations. The collection of customs duties is relatively simple, yet there is still the issue of unchecked smuggling today. How much more complex is income tax, and the situation is almost ten times that of customs duties. In addition to the special circumstances in North China, there are still so-called registered residents in Shantou and Xiamen, which are sufficient to hinder future tax collection. Not only foreign nationals, not only concessions, and not only foreign banks, if they cannot all be brought into compliance, reckless collection will lead to cunning people competing to evade taxes, and the national wealth will be transferred to foreign coffers. The state's revenue will be minimal, and its vitality will be almost exhausted. Without considering the risk of presumption, the affiliated associations have made earnest requests in their telegrams some days ago. Now, each of the chambers of commerce attending this conference has appointed one representative to prepare a petition and respectfully submit everything to your department, hoping for your review and approval to eliminate disguised likin taxes in various provinces by a set deadline, and to complete the procedures for uniformly collecting income tax from foreign nationals in advance, so that the collection of income tax will be simultaneous and equal for Chinese and foreign residents, without priority or distinction, in order to conform to the noble intention of your department to strive to promote good taxes. How can we not urgently await your orders! Respectfully submitted to the Ministry of Finance.

Salt Affairs Administration: Improving Salt Administration

Preparing to Implement the New Salt Law

Shenshi News Agency reports that since the promulgation of the new salt law last year, the Salt Affairs Administration has first rectified the working guidelines of salt fields in various provinces, proceeding according to the two principles of free trade and on-site tax collection of the new salt law, and actively improving the balance of production and sales and tax revenue. The organization's plan for promoting the new salt law is recorded as follows:

Matters for Rectification

China's salt administration has adhered to old methods for thousands of years, and it is still not sound, which has a significant impact on national tax revenue and people's food. Since the promulgation of the new salt law last year, the Salt Affairs Administration has decided to thoroughly reform the salt administration, cancel the division of shores, reorganize salt fields, ban local saltpeter salt, standardize quality, and improve the lives of salt farmers, all of which are matters that urgently need to be rectified in today's salt administration.

Reorganizing Salt Fields

China's salt fields are very scattered and difficult to manage, and it is extremely difficult to collect taxes on-site, which is bound to lead to tax evasion. Therefore, reorganizing salt fields is the most important task, which is to merge salt fields and build warehouses. The indispensable steps are three: (1) Investigate salt field production and survey salt field areas, making a detailed report on the area of salt fields, the number of warehouses, transportation, production costs, salt quality, and the lives of salt farmers, and then study reorganization methods based on this report. (2) Merge salt fields and establish salt fields. Many salt fields have low yields, high costs, weak brine, and overly fragmented plots. These salt fields should be abolished and arrangements should be made for the resettlement of unemployed salt farmers in the abolished areas, while providing relief to salt farmers, transforming salt into agriculture, and opening up ponds and ditches in salt fields, diverting water to dilute the soil, improving the soil, and converting salt into reclamation. (3) Build warehouses and repair roads and open ditches to improve salt field management and avoid tax evasion.

Improving Manufacturing

China's salt production has always adhered to ancient methods, with little improvement. Therefore, the salt quality is very poor. However, in the future, with the implementation of the new salt law, free trade, and the breaking of the salt transport permit system, inferior salt will inevitably be difficult to sell competitively. Therefore, improving manufacturing is essential: (1) Inspect salt quality to promote manufacturing improvement. (2) Abandon boiling and switch to sun drying to reduce salt production costs. (3) Improve the technology of coarse salt manufacturing to improve the quality of group salt. (4) Promote refined salt to seek material progress.

Banning Inferior Salt

In addition to sea salt, pond salt, and well salt, China's salt production also includes gypsum salt, saltpeter salt, and local salt. Among them, local saltpeter and local salt are not only produced in a very wide area, but also extremely scattered. The sodium chloride content of the salt is mostly below 60%. Using it as edible salt is not only harmful to hygiene but also infringes on national taxes. Therefore, it is often strictly prohibited.

Recent Rectification Status

In addition to improving salt field production, the Salt Affairs Administration is also striving to improve the lives of salt farmers and balance tax rates, providing salt farmer loans, and providing relief to salt farmers' livelihoods. It is reported that the Changlu and Lianghuai salt fields are about to complete matters such as building salt pits and improving quality, and the new salt law may be implemented first. The salt fields in Zhejiang, Shandong, Fujian, Guangdong, and other places are currently in a period of active rectification. It is expected that the nationwide implementation of the new salt law, on-site tax collection, and free trade will not be far off.

Agreed Measures for Banning Opium in Concession Areas Scheduled for Joint Implementation in August, Our Side in Charge of Supervision and Concession Areas Responsible for Implementation, General Reporting Deadline, and Offenders to be Punished According to Law

Dagong News Agency reports that in order to promote the work of banning opium and drugs in concession areas, the government's Standing Committee has, through the military commission's special envoy Ma Liang, in conjunction with Mayor Wu, obtained concrete approaches after consulting with the concession authorities based on the regulations stipulated by the central government. Implementation is scheduled to begin on August 10. The special envoy's office will continue to work to supervise the concession area's opium ban. Dagong News Agency's reporter has learned the details as follows:

Implementing the Opium Ban in Concession Areas After the military commission issued an order to the Shanghai-based special envoy's office and the municipal government to implement measures to ban opium and drugs in concession areas, Special Envoy Ma Liang and Mayor Wu discussed the steps for implementing the ban. The concession authorities have now expressed their support for our side's agreed measures to ban opium. The Municipal Council and the Board of Directors are the implementing agencies, the courts are the punishing agencies, and the special envoy's office and the municipal government are the supervising agencies. The registration of opium users is handled by the police stations in each district, and the Municipal Council will designate hospitals within the concession to be responsible for sending opium users to quit opium. The administrative procedures are the same as those handled by the Municipal Public Security Bureau. However, the supervisory agencies have the power of supervision and consultation over the opium ban in the concession areas and will cooperate in the process. As for the date for completely eliminating opium and drugs, it will be completely eradicated within the time limit stipulated by our central authorities. It was originally planned to jointly establish an opium ban agency in the concession areas, but because the concession authorities could not agree, the matter has been temporarily suspended.

Starting Next Month After repeated consultations between the two parties, the measures for implementing the opium ban in the concession areas have achieved a solution. The competent authorities are submitting these agreed measures to the Opium Ban General Association and the General Supervision Department for review. If there are no changes, it has been decided that implementation will begin on August 10. The first step is to carry out registration and licensing. The second step is to carry out reporting. The third step is to enforce compulsory rehabilitation. When the implementation period begins, a joint notice will be issued by the municipal government, the special envoy's office, the Municipal Council, and the Board of Directors to inform the public.

Attention Opium Users Since the Municipal Public Security Bureau, in compliance with the order of the military commission's General Supervision Department, began the city-wide general reporting work on May 10, there are only ten days left until the deadline of August 10 as stipulated. During the reporting period, more than 12,000 opium users have registered retroactively. After the end of the general reporting work, if unregistered opium users or those who traffic, produce, or sell drugs are found, they will be severely punished according to law.

Guo Bingwen Speaks on International Trade

Opinions After the Investigation

A reporter from Xinsheng News Agency interviewed Guo Bingwen, Director of the International Trade Bureau, yesterday to inquire about the international trade situation after his investigation abroad. According to him, the report in the newspaper (note that this newspaper did not publish it yesterday) about the international trade sections of my speech at the local association contained many inaccuracies. He agreed to give a summary of the original manuscript of his speech at that time, as follows: In addition to investigating international trade, I also studied the silver issue in the United States during this trip. It was found that after the implementation of the silver bill in the United States, the facts were completely opposite to its ideals. Therefore, even those who supported the silver policy changed their attitudes. The government was in a dilemma and thought about jointly discussing the matter with silver-producing and silver-using countries, and invited our country to participate. After seven weeks of discussion, our side agreed to increase the silver shake-off, and the US side used US dollars to exchange for Chinese silver, so that our country's new currency, which has tended to stabilize, is even more consolidated, and the international finance is gradually stabilized as a result. Moreover, the recession in the United States has gradually disappeared, and there is hope for further progress in trade between China and the United States. As for the state of our country's foreign trade, it can be divided into three points: one is handicrafts, one is major agricultural products, and one is manufactured goods. Handicrafts have always been welcomed by Europeans and Americans, but because they have adhered to old methods for decades and have failed to cater to the psychology of foreigners, their business is declining and there is already a phenomenon of being replaced by others. As far as I know, Chinese silk used to account for 50% of the total imports to the United States, but it gradually decreased due to Japanese silk competition. Last year, it only accounted for 2%. Fifty years ago, tea accounted for 90% of the total imports to the United States, but last year it dropped to 6% due to competition from Indian and Japanese tea. However, tung oil, due to the surge in demand, the amount exported to the United States last year, considering only the paint industry, was worth more than 30 million yuan. However, due to its impure quality, unstable output, and fluctuating prices, the US Department of Commerce and the Tung Oil Association have advocated planting tung trees, and there are already products that are not inferior to Chinese products. South America, Africa, the Soviet Union, and British colonies are also encouraging planting tung trees, which will inevitably affect the sales of tung oil in our country in the future. Therefore, Minister Wu of the Ministry of Industry has recently planned to establish a vegetable oil refining plant, and also intends to improve the production and sales methods of silk, tea, and so on, and gradually promote them. It is not difficult to restore sales. Domestically produced manufactured goods have considerable strength in Nanyang, Singapore, and other places, but the promotion has not been effective, and domestic manufacturers do not have sound organizations. For example, the silk fabrics of the Meiya Factory and domestically produced light bulbs and electric fans all have the potential for promotion, but they cannot be promoted due to the lack of places to buy them. The Philippines and other places also have the same situation. I hope that the colleagues of this association and domestic manufacturers will pay attention to it. In short, for foreign trade, (1) the goods should be of high quality and strive for progress, and standardization is necessary. (2) The price should be low, so that it can compete with other similar goods in the market. (3) A three-legged sound sales organization. (4) Financial institutions should provide exporters with financial convenience. (5) The government should bear greater advocacy and guidance, such as the Trade Bureau established by the US government, which has 25 branch offices in the country, 54 cooperative institutions, and 33 commercial counselors and commissioners stationed abroad. It also has an import and export industry bank, which specializes in lending for foreign trade. The lending period is usually one to five years, and it can be extended in special circumstances. The United Kingdom, France, Germany, Italy, and other countries have even more loan insurance institutions for trade, and many other countries have followed suit, which can all be learned from our country. In addition, there are many ways to restrict imports and encourage exports, such as implementing protective tariffs, controlling foreign exchange, revising reciprocal commercial treaties, international clearing agreements, and commodity exchanges, which can also be studied by our country and selectively implemented.

Ye Xiasheng Arrived in Shanghai from Beijing Last Night

Waiting for a Ship to Guangdong to Take Office

In order to thoroughly rectify the judicial affairs of Guangdong Province, the central government has appointed Ye Xiasheng as the President of the Guangdong High Court. After being appointed, Ye visited President Ju and Minister Wang in Beijing to ask for instructions on everything. He left Beijing by night train on the 23rd and arrived in Shanghai, waiting for a ship to Guangdong to take office. According to reports, Ye is 48 years old, originally from Binhai, Zhejiang, and grew up in Panyu, Guangdong. During the late Qing Dynasty, he studied in Japan and joined the revolutionary work. After returning to China, he served as the supervisor of the Guangdong Law and Politics School, followed Sun Yat-sen to advocate the revolution, and participated in the Huanghuagang and Longhumen battles. After the restoration of Guangdong, he served as the Director of the Judicial Department and the Director of the Education Department. When Sun Yat-sen took office as the Extraordinary President in Nanjing, he served as the Secretary of the Presidential Palace, and then served as the Negotiator in Jiujiang and was elected as a member of the House of Representatives. In the fourth year of the Republic, he followed Sun Yat-sen to the east and served as the Prime Minister's Secretary, drafting the party platform of the Chinese Revolutionary Party. During the Guardian of the Constitution Movement, he served as the Secretary of the Marshal's Office, concurrently as the Director of the Ministry of Internal Affairs and Acting Minister. In recent years, he has been practicing law in Guangdong and has been deeply disgusted with the darkness of the judicial system in Guangdong. This appointment is expected to bring about improvements in the judicial affairs of Guangdong in the future.

Eurasia Company Implements Through Airline Service

Giant Aircraft Available at All Times, Without Conflicts with Other Lines

In order to connect all lines and implement airline network transportation, the Eurasia Aviation Company has allocated the Junkers giant aircraft leased from the German Lufthansa Company to the Shanghai-Yunnan, Shaanxi-Yunnan, and Lanzhou-Baotou lines, specializing in round-trip long-distance flights. The Shanghai station is the starting and ending point. The flight itinerary is: (1) Outbound flight departs from Shanghai, via Nanjing, Zhengzhou, directly to Xi'an, Chengdu, and Kunming. Then, from Kunming, it flies via Chengdu and Xi'an to Lanzhou, and then from Lanzhou it flies to Ningxia and Baotou. (2) The return flight departs from Baotou, via Ningxia, Lanzhou, Xi'an, Zhengzhou, Nanjing, and directly to Shanghai. There are two flights per week. This through flight method has been implemented since today. In addition to the giant aircraft previously leased from Germany, which has already been flying this through line, the giant aircraft that recently arrived in Shanghai will also officially join the flight next Tuesday. Another giant aircraft that will arrive soon will also be allocated to the through line in the future, so that these three giant aircraft will fly in shifts according to the schedule. As for the original other aircraft, they will still fly on various lines as usual, without conflicting with the through line.

Ministry of Communications Attaches Importance to Navigation Safety and Rectifies Ship Radios

Formulates Five Rectification Measures and Orders All Merchant Ships to Comply

The Ministry of Communications, in view of the fact that the ship radio equipment established by various Chinese merchant ships is simple and poorly maintained, resulting in reduced communication efficiency, which is of great importance to navigation safety, now the Ministry has formulated five rectification measures to improve the communication efficiency of various ship radios. The details are as follows: (1) When each Chinese merchant ship equipped with a ship radio arrives in Shanghai, the captain or his agent shall immediately report in writing to the Shanghai Maritime Affairs Bureau, which shall notify the Shanghai International Radio Station to select an engineer or technician to go for inspection. (2) When the International Radio Station's technician inspects the ship's radio, he shall pay attention to the following points: A. Whether the transmitting and receiving equipment is maintained perfectly; B. Whether the power supply equipment is suitable; C. Whether the transmitting frequency is accurate; D. Whether the antenna method and height and length are appropriate; E. Whether there is a spare transceiver and automatic alarm; F. Whether the battery is maintained perfectly; G. Whether the radio room location and equipment are appropriate; H. Whether the radio station and radio officer have licenses and how many radio officers there are; I. Whether the radio compass is accurate; J. Other matters related to communication efficiency. (3) After the International Radio Station's inspector completes the inspection, he shall immediately fill out four copies of the inspection report, one copy shall be submitted to the Ministry of Communications for verification, one copy shall be sent to the Maritime Affairs Bureau for record, one copy shall be given to the captain or his agent for reference, and one copy shall be kept by the radio station. (4) If the inspection report contains any discrepancies in the ship's radio equipment, the Maritime Affairs Bureau shall supervise the ship to quickly rectify and improve it. (5) After the ship's radio has been improved, the Maritime Affairs Bureau shall be immediately notified in writing, and the Bureau shall notify the International Radio Station to send personnel to re-inspect it. If any discrepancies are still found, the measures stipulated in Article 4 shall be followed.

Hua Yang Yi Zhen Hui Reports on the Tragic Situation of the Flood in Shanghang

The Hua Yang Yi Zhen Hui at No. 97 Renji Road received a letter from the Shanghang County Flood Relief Association in Fujian Province, which is copied below, "Alas, Heaven has brought disaster to the people of Hang, causing successive catastrophes. After the Red bandits, they have suffered from a flood. They are scattered and displaced, and it is shocking and heartbreaking. According to reports from various districts in the county, since the middle of May this year, it has been raining heavily and continuously. Mountain floods have risen sharply everywhere, overflowing and flooding. The fields and crops are all submerged, and the waterway in the Tingjiang River basin is blocked. It has been more than ten days, and the disaster is becoming more and more urgent, and the disaster is becoming more and more apparent. The most serious disaster is in the Dayang Dam, Xiaxia Suqian and other villages in the eastern district, and the Gutian Qiufang Zhongcun Sukeng Xiadaohu area in the northern district. Many houses and livestock have been washed away, and the fields and seedlings have been turned into gravel. The bridges and roads along the river have been completely destroyed, with losses of no less than tens of thousands of yuan. The most tragic thing is that all the shops in the Dayang Dam market were washed away by the flood. In Jinghuang Village, there were only two stoves for seventy households, and corpses covered the river for days without ceasing. The Dayang Dam is located in the upper reaches of the Hangdong River and has never suffered from floods before. This time, the disaster is particularly serious, so the losses in the lower reaches can be imagined. The number of buildings that were washed away, such as the Tabamu Bridge, cannot be built for less than three or four thousand gold, and other losses are countless. The most painful and pitiful thing is that the people in the disaster area, excluding those who were buried in the bellies of fish, are displaced and have nothing to live on. They are disheveled and barefoot, living in the open air, supporting the old and carrying the young, begging in other villages, crying for help, and lamenting everywhere. It is not necessary to draw Zheng Xia's picture, it is enough to make those who hear it sad. Moreover, the price of rice in this county is as precious as pearls due to the impact of the flood, and the rice fields in the disaster area have been completely destroyed and there is no harvest. If no measures are taken to provide relief, then tens of thousands of disaster victims will not only avoid being killed on the road, but will also die of starvation in autumn and winter. The colleagues were heartbroken by what they saw, so they organized a relief association to plan and manage the relief efforts. They have already submitted a request to the government to allocate funds for relief. However, it is difficult to expect a living fish from a distant river, and at a time when public funds are extremely tight, whether the government can allocate as much relief as possible is still a guess. In order to seek quick results, we have to recommend enthusiastic fellow villagers from this county and various places abroad to sponsor fundraising and directly appeal to charitable figures at home and abroad to ask for help. It is said that natural disasters occur everywhere, and it is also said that everyone likes to do good, who is not as good as me? We humbly ask benevolent gentlemen to have a compassionate heart and to accomplish a broad and generous act, generously donating money to provide relief, so that those who receive the relief will not only bathe in the grace of rebirth, but the entire people of Hangzhou will also pay tribute to the boundless gift."

Rice Pile Collapses and Injures Many People, Shop Assistants and Passers-by Were Also Injured, None Seriously, and Were Bandaged and Discharged from the Hospital

The Yichengyuan Grain Store at the intersection of Xinjiang Road and Guoqing Road, due to a large batch of machine-milled rice transported from other places the previous evening (the 23rd), the shop assistants Yang Jinsheng and others piled it up overnight in the corridor along the door outside the counter in the store. It was not finished until after 8 p.m. At that time, a loud noise was suddenly heard. Because the rice pile was piled too high, the signboard could not withstand it and collapsed towards the road. At that time, there were a dozen children from Jiangbei gathered along the door of the store, sweeping up the remaining rice. Several of them were injured because they could not avoid it. A passer-by was also injured in the left leg. Afterwards, the shop assistants immediately called an ambulance and sent the injured people to the Hongguang Red Cross Hospital. Because the injuries were minor, they were bandaged and then sent to the Menggu Road Police Station in the same car. After questioning, they were released. The names of the injured people at the time are copied below: (1) Sun Youcai (28 years old), injured in the left leg; (2) Zhou Guisheng (9 years old), injured in the face; (3) Xu Chengfeng (15 years old), injured in the leg; (4) Xu Chenglong (9 years old), injured in the face; (5) Wu Xiaowuzi (5 years old), injured in the face; (6) Yang Jinsheng (shop assistant of the rice store), injured in the face.

Local Customs

Studying Sanskrit

Shanghai First Special District Court Plans to Establish a Notary Office, Scheduled to Open on August 1

The Provisional Rules for Notarization were previously promulgated by the Judicial Yuan in July last year. It is reported that the Shanghai First Special District Court has been ordered to establish a Notary Office to handle notarization affairs. It is currently preparing and is scheduled to be officially established on August 1. The Ministry of Justice has designated a judge from the court to specialize in notarization affairs, and there are several court clerks to assist in handling. In the future, parties can request notarization for legal acts or other facts concerning private rights, or for private documents that have been made, and may appoint an agent to do so. Copies of notarized documents and authenticated private documents are not subject to loss. In the event of litigation, they can be submitted for reference at any time or requested by the court for review. Public documents created at the Notary Office can avoid problems arising when they are cited as evidence due to non-compliance with the form. (However, if a party knows that a matter is false and requests notarization or authentication that is sufficient to harm the rights of others, he shall be liable for criminal liability.) Moreover, according to Article 11 of the Provisional Rules for Notarization, a notarized document stating the name of the direct enforcement can be obtained without litigation procedures, eliminating many disputes. It is reported that the Detailed Rules for the Implementation of the Provisional Rules for Notarization and the Rules for Notarization Fees, etc., are currently being printed urgently to prepare for people to ask for them.

Directorate General of Posts, Nationwide: Filming Postal Movies to Popularize Postal Knowledge Among the People

In order to develop the postal service and disseminate knowledge of postal transportation, convenience, and stability to the people, especially those in remote areas, the Ministry of Transportation has ordered the Directorate General of Posts to produce postal movies. Various postal bureaus, postal savings and remittance bureaus in provinces, cities, and districts have collected materials on daily postal and savings/remittance operations, including mail, remittances, savings, and other tasks, and have been filming them by category. The filming is nearing completion and is scheduled to begin touring and screening in September along the Beijing-Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo railway lines, as well as in various ports and towns. The screening locations will be selected by the local post offices. Admission to the screenings will be free of charge. Subsequently, screenings will be held in all locations with post offices to achieve nationwide popularization.

Category B Diesel: Revised Tax Collection Method, Jianghai Customs Announces for General Knowledge

Jianghai Customs issued Announcement No. 1530 to announce the revised method for collecting taxes on Category B diesel based on the actual kerosene content ratio: Regarding the case of proportional taxation on imported Category B diesel, it was previously ordered that diesel with a kerosene content exceeding 60% would be subject to proportional taxation. Upon customs verification, a tax of 33.60 gold units per ton would be levied, as proportional to 60% diesel, with the diesel tax capped at 80% of the kerosene tax. This was announced in Announcement No. 1351 on March 31, 1934. Now, in accordance with the Ministry of Finance's order, all mineral oils that are classified as Category B diesel for tax purposes shall be taxed according to the actual kerosene content ratio. The original stipulation that the tax should be capped at 80% of the kerosene tax is hereby cancelled, effective July 1, 1936. All merchants are hereby notified. Supervisor Tang Hai'an, Customs Commissioner Ba Guisen.

Vagrant Assault and Murder of Policeman Case at Shanghai Vagrant Labor Camp: Sentencing Set for the 28th

Vagrants Gao Fuxiang, Pan Heshou, Hong Jianfu, and others from the Caohejing Vagrant Labor Camp, along with fugitives Yao Benren, Gao Yongling, Wu Ruilin, and others, conspired to escape and assaulted and killed guard Lu Yecai. Another guard noticed this and quickly summoned other guards to surround and arrest Gao Fuxiang, Pan Heshou, and Hong Jianfu. Yao Benren, Gao Yongling, Wu Ruilin, and others escaped. They were handed over to the Mountain District Court for investigation and prosecution for murder under Article 271, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law. After repeated review by Judge Zhao Yongzhou, another continued hearing was held at 10 a.m. yesterday. Defendants Gao Fuxiang and Pan Heshou confessed to the joint assault but claimed that it was Yao Benren and others who initiated the escape due to unbearable suffering in the labor camp, and they merely echoed their sentiments. However, Hong Jianfu claimed that he voluntarily entered the camp to learn a skill, did not want to escape, and therefore was not part of the conspiracy. He stated that he did not stop the others at the time out of fear of violence, but he did not escape afterward, which could serve as proof. At this point, the prosecutor presented his arguments, stating that the defendants had confessed and that the murder of the guard occurred in their room, so it was determined that there was evidence of their guilt and requested that they be convicted. Subsequently, defense lawyers Xu Heling and Sun Zhiwu each presented legal arguments. The presiding judge declared the arguments concluded and set the sentencing for the 28th of this month.

Public Concession Has Over 40,000 Rickshaw Pullers; Crackdown on Unlicensed Rickshaws Intensified

According to the recent report of the Rickshaw Affairs Committee of the Public Works Department, the number of rickshaw pullers in the Public Concession who have renewed their licenses is 36,045. In addition, there are 4,992 newly licensed pullers. Therefore, the authorities believe that the current number of pullers is sufficient to meet the needs of the rickshaw industry. The police have been entrusted to make every effort to ensure that all rickshaw pullers in the city have licenses and wear armbands. Furthermore, there are now 1,921 new-style rickshaws on the market, providing passengers with greater comfort than before.

Regarding the issue of rickshaw owners overcharging rent, another case occurred in June. However, the reporting puller was absent from the negotiations. After investigation, it was discovered that the rickshaw owner had bribed them to be absent. Later, the pullers reported to the Vehicle Affairs Committee again because the rickshaw owner did not fulfill his previous promises, but the Vehicle Affairs Committee rejected the report. In addition to issuing a stern warning to the rickshaw owner, a judgment was not made for the time being. However, recently, the licenses of four rickshaw owners were revoked for overcharging rent, which has greatly helped to standardize rickshaw rentals.

Furthermore, regarding private rickshaws, there are so-called unlicensed chartered rickshaws in the city. Although the police authorities have severely cracked down on them, they have not been completely eliminated. This matter was recently discussed again by the Special Rickshaw Committee, which stated that the police should be responsible for intensifying investigations and that the true purpose of those who obtain private rickshaw licenses must be determined. If any violations occur, the rickshaw owner should be made aware of their responsibilities. If a rickshaw puller violates the regulations twice, their license will be permanently revoked.

New Life Movement Promotion Association Ordered to Eliminate Extra Tips

Meeting Scheduled for the 27th; Implementation After Decision

The New Life Movement Promotion Association has formulated implementation measures to eliminate extra tips and has ordered New Life Movement Associations in various regions to promote and implement them. The New Life Movement Association of this city, after receiving the order, has scheduled a meeting of relevant agencies and organizations for the 27th of this month to discuss the measures. Details are recorded below.

The New Life Movement Promotion Association of this city has been ordered by the General Association that due to the unlimited tipping practices in various hotels, teahouses, restaurants, eateries, barbershops, bathhouses, theaters, cinemas, and other public entertainment venues, waiters arbitrarily demand tips, making it difficult for guests to pay and often provoking disputes between hosts and guests, which seriously violates the regulations of the New Life Movement, the Association has formulated "Implementation Measures for the Elimination of Extra Tips" and distributed them to New Life Movement Associations in various regions for promotion and implementation in order to eliminate these bad practices. In addition to notifying them separately, the Association has sent the measures for review and implementation, and to report the implementation status at any time. After receiving the order, the Association has scheduled a meeting of representatives from relevant agencies and organizations for 10:00 a.m. on the 27th of this month (Monday) at the Maple Bridge Association to discuss the implementation measures.

Implementation Measures: The implementation measures for eliminating extra tips are as follows: (1) Scope: All hotels, teahouses, restaurants, eateries, bathhouses, barbershops, theaters, various stores, and those who have extra tips in all locations are subject to elimination. The measures are as follows: (2) Principles: 1. The principle of operating income for various stores is not to collect tips. 2. During the trial period, except for temporarily allowing the cashier to collect one tip, it is absolutely forbidden to ask guests for extra tips. 3. All waiters and workers in various industries are given fixed salaries by the owners, and the distribution of one tip collected is voluntarily agreed upon by the owners and workers. 4. If extra tips are demanded, the guest should refuse directly. If they are forced to demand them again, they can report to the nearby military and police agencies for punishment. 5. In addition to one tip, guests must not give extra tips. At the same time, waiters and workers must also decline when guests give tips, otherwise, once verified, they will be punished according to regulations. (3) Steps: 1. Preparation: The following agencies and organizations will jointly discuss the implementation: 1. New Life Movement Association, 2. Party Headquarters, 3. Government, 4. Chamber of Commerce, 5. Various Industry Associations, 6. Military and Police Agencies. 2. Implementation: 1. First, the tip elimination measures will be printed and published according to the distribution of public security agencies, ordering the owners of each store to comply. 2. Ten days after the tip elimination measures are printed and published, a inspection team will be organized by the New Life Movement Association and military and police agency personnel to implement the inspection. (4) Rewards and Punishments: 1. Representatives from various agencies and organizations will jointly discuss and agree on reward and punishment covenants and notify various industries to implement them. 2. Reward and punishment methods are as follows: 1. Reward: Issue certificates of merit, reward by publishing in the newspaper, or other methods. 2. Punishment: Warnings, fines, business suspensions, or other methods. (5) Supplementary Provisions: These measures will be announced by the General Association of the New Life Movement and implemented.

French Concession Reregisters Traditional Chinese Medicine Practitioners; Traditional Chinese Medicine Organizations Oppose

Sending Letters Requesting Assistance

Traditional Chinese medicine practitioners practicing in Shanghai have been examined and qualified by the Municipal Health Bureau and issued licenses. However, those residing in the special zone must register with the authorities again. The Second Special District, after agreeing with the Traditional Chinese Medicine Organization in 1931, determined that registration would be valid for life. Unexpectedly, the "Regulations for Managing the Practice of Traditional Chinese Medicine" were recently promulgated, changing the validity period to five years and increasing the registration fee from two yuan to five yuan. There are also items such as health donations and investigation fees. A slight delay will result in fines. As a result, traditional Chinese medicine practitioners in the district have reported to the Shanghai Traditional Chinese Medicine Association, the Shanghai Traditional Chinese Medicine Society, the Chinese Traditional Chinese Medicine Society, and the Shenzhou Traditional Chinese Medicine Society, requesting negotiations to abolish the new regulations and improve treatment. The associations have also jointly discussed and decided to negotiate with the French authorities, and have jointly sent letters to the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau, the French Concession Board of Directors, the Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Second Special District, and Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, Lu Bohong, Qi Yunqing, Zhang Jixian, Qian Xinzhi, etc., requesting assistance, and have published notices in the newspaper to members, reporting the situation. The original letters to the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau, the French Concession Board of Directors, and the Chinese Directors of the Taxpayers' Association are recorded as follows: "Respected Sirs, Our associations have repeatedly received complaints from members residing in the Second Special District of this city, stating that the French Board of Works recently promulgated the "Regulations for Managing the Practice of Traditional Chinese Medicine" under Order No. 58 of the French Consul General, requiring all traditional Chinese medicine practitioners, regardless of whether they have registered or not, to reregister in accordance with the regulations. Not only has the fee doubled, but also the procedures have become cumbersome. Other items such as health donations and investigation fees will be fined for a slight delay. During normal inspections, foreign translators often arrive with aggressive postures, making it difficult for freelance professionals to endure oppression. The cost of living is high, making it difficult to bear the burden. We request negotiations and assistance to abolish the new regulations and improve treatment, etc." They have come to the association one after another for the same reason. According to the members, they are all traditional Chinese medicine practitioners who have been formally registered by your bureau (Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau), reside in the Second Special District, and have already paid business taxes (that is, a health donation of two yuan per year). They should not be subject to other forced restrictions. (Doctor registration in the First Special District is at the discretion of the doctors.) In 1931, when the French Concession first implemented doctor registration, our associations negotiated, and as a result, the French authorities solemnly announced that after one registration, it would be valid for life. Only then did everyone endure and make concessions and register in accordance with the regulations. However, not long after, they went back on their word and showed no integrity. Suddenly, the "Regulations for Managing the Practice of Traditional Chinese Medicine" were promulgated, not only changing the term from life to five years and increasing the fee from two yuan to five yuan, but also increasing the burden that traditional Chinese medicine practitioners should not bear, such as health donations and investigation fees, and depriving the freedom of the traditional Chinese medicine profession in every way possible. For the sake of maintaining the business of our members, we have been entrusted by the majority and have no choice but to make the following appeals on their behalf: (1) The doctor registration held by the French Concession in 1930 generally refers to Western medicine, traditional Chinese medicine, dentistry, and veterinary medicine. Today, it only concerns our traditional Chinese medicine practitioners. It is not called the Traditional Chinese Medicine Registration Regulations, but the Regulations for Managing the Practice of Traditional Chinese Medicine. Looking at the name, its meaning is clear. Although the special zone is called a concession, there is still freedom of occupation. Today, only traditional Chinese medicine practitioners residing in the French Concession, in addition to being governed by their own government, must also bear the dual obligations of the French Concession (in addition to business tax and health donations, there is now a registration fee every five years, hence the dual obligation). Is it fair? (2) The new regulations state that when registering, in addition to the business license of the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau as proof, proof of date of birth, nationality, and place of origin is also required (Item 1 of Article 2). This proof is naturally not available to Chinese people, will it not cause difficulties during registration? This is also one of the cumbersome procedures. (3) Article 11 of the new regulations states that "the business of traditional Chinese medicine practitioners should be limited to the behavior within the scope of their industry as usual," while Article 12 has the harsh restriction that "traditional Chinese medicine practitioners must not prepare or sell medicines or partner with pharmacists or traditional Chinese medicine merchants without special permission." Will not the commonly used medicines of surgeons, injury departments, and internal medicine departments be subject to unnecessary restrictions and unable to carry out their business? The prohibition of partnership is a deprivation of the freedom of business, which is not found in any rule of law. (4) Article 14 of the new regulations states that "traditional Chinese medicine practitioners must not move their clinics without prior notification to the Director of the Health Department of the French Board of Works." The original intention of this provision is not known, but when this article is implemented, it will inevitably cause many disputes and difficulties. This provision is difficult to comply with. (5) The application form for registration in Article 2 must be paid for, and the amount of donations in Article 8 and the donations for extension in Article 10 are not specified. It was originally intended to be a one-time lifetime, but now it is changed to once every five years. However, how much gold will each person have to bear in these five years? In this time of economic depression and the decline of all industries, it is unbearable. (6) Article 10 of the new regulations, which states that "the validity period of the business license is five years," clearly means that it must be reregistered every five years. Judging from the statement "limited to the donation of ...", it can be subtly implied that the purpose is entirely to collect money. The profession of traditional Chinese medicine is inherently free, and the nature of traditional Chinese medicine is close to charity. In terms of health administration, it is naturally beneficial and harmless. Why should traditional Chinese medicine practitioners residing in the French Concession be subject to such heavy restrictions and burdens? If the French authorities are not imposing a ban in disguise, it is discriminating against traditional Chinese medicine. In short, the promulgation of the new regulations is neither beneficial in law nor in sentiment. All our traditional Chinese medicine practitioners cannot bear it. We have specifically made this statement and implore your bureau to fight for justice and forward it to the French Concession Board of Directors. (Taxpayers' Association) Your esteemed association advocates fairness and forwards it to the Board of Directors of (the Board of Directors) Your esteemed board quickly complies with public opinion, sympathizes with the difficulties, withdraws the order, and restores trust in accordance with past practices. We cannot but wait for orders with the utmost urgency."

Black Smoke from Yangshupu Power Plant - Commercial Remedy Measures

Achieving the goal within eighteen months

The Shanghai Power Company's plant in Yangshupu has been releasing black smoke from its chimneys, causing dissatisfaction among nearby businesses and residents. They have repeatedly requested the Municipal Council to take measures to address this issue. The Municipal Council's relevant departments, such as the Works and Health departments, have discussed this matter with the company's management on several occasions. According to the company's management, this issue has long been a concern for the company, and they have hired experts to conduct various experiments to reduce smoke. However, due to the unique circumstances of this area, it is difficult to achieve complete success in the short term. Nevertheless, they will continue to make efforts to achieve a satisfactory outcome. Recently, the Municipal Council has repeatedly negotiated with the company's management, urging them to make every effort to eliminate smoke emissions. The Municipal Council's departments have also proposed several measures, which the power company has sympathetically accepted. However, due to economic considerations, they are not planning to invest heavily in other remedial work until the current experimental results are fully confirmed. Recently, the Municipal Council's Defense Committee convened a meeting, inviting company representatives to discuss this issue. The company provided a very detailed report on the progress of recent remedial work. The committee resolved to urge the company management to expedite the implementation of the measures they have outlined and to submit regular reports to the Municipal Council on the progress and effectiveness of these measures. The Works Department will also be responsible for regular inspections. The ongoing experiments are expected to be completed by the end of November, at which time the Works Department will submit an inspection report. The goal is to completely eliminate black smoke emissions within a year and a half. Regarding the raising of the chimneys, opinions are divided on its effectiveness. However, in the future, when new plants are built, the chimneys should be higher than the existing ones. The currently decided remedial measures will still be implemented to ensure their effectiveness. It is said that the above measures have all been approved by the Municipal Council's Board of Directors.

International Swimming Competition Held at the Municipal Swimming Pool on the Evenings of August 8th and 9th

The fifth International Swimming Competition, an informal meeting, was held yesterday afternoon at the West YMCA. Attendees included Mr. Hexlett, President of the Shanghai Inter-Port Swimming Association; Mr. Brock, Secretary; Mr. Brock representing the West YMCA; Mr. Yu Binqi representing China; and Mr. Motoyama from Japan. Mr. Hexlett first reported that the Inter-Port Swimming Competition would be held in Tianjin at the end of August, and Shanghai's representatives could be outstanding athletes from this international competition. There is no shortage of talent from China, Japan, Britain, the United States, France, and Russia. People of all nationalities in Shanghai must take responsibility and raise funds to send representatives. It is proposed to use the income from this International Swimming Competition to cover the travel expenses of the Inter-Port representatives. A meeting was previously convened to decide to hold it at the French Chamber of Commerce, as their swimming pool has more seats, which would generate more revenue. Mr. Brock strongly supported this, but Mr. Yu Binqi strongly opposed it. He pointed out that the French Chamber of Commerce swimming pool is 60 yards long, which does not meet the standard. The Shanghai Municipal Swimming Pool was originally built by Mayor Wu for the people of Shanghai to swim. This time, it should be held at the Municipal Swimming Pool to honor Mayor Wu's advocacy. Moreover, the pool's length, width, and all equipment are the best in East Asia. At this point, Mr. Motoyama, the Japanese representative, stood up and proposed, quite supportive, and said that since Shanghai has a swimming pool and its equipment is perfect, it is very suitable to be held at the Municipal Swimming Pool. China, as the host country, should take the responsibility. As a result, it was passed unanimously. The competition date is scheduled for 8:30 PM on the evenings of August 8th and 9th. It is reported that Mr. Yu Binqi, because the matter is international and of great responsibility, plans to go to the China National Sports Association today to seek advice, visit Mayor Wu, Director Pan, and the Municipal Sports Field, and ask for instructions before convening the Chinese Swimming Committee to discuss the preliminary selection of the Chinese team and determine the dates of the competition events.

Educational News

Recent Trends in Central Educational Administration: Higher Education Focuses on Practical Subjects with Marked Success; Improving Secondary Schools, Implementing Compulsory Education, and Promoting Private Schools

(Nanjing Special Dispatch) In the past three years, the Ministry of Education has made many reforms to education at all levels. The facts are scattered in various newspapers, but Minister Wang Shijie has devoted himself to hard work and rarely expresses his opinions on educational administration to reporters. Senior officials in the ministry also follow this principle, and rarely provide systematic explanations of administrative matters. As the 24th year has ended and the 25th year has begun, the reporter will provide a systematic description of the recent trends in central educational administration.

In terms of higher education, the policy in recent years has been to narrow the scope and enrich the content, not to pursue quantitative development, but to improve the quality. Efforts are made to avoid extravagance and decoration and to focus on pragmatism. In recent years, the merging of repetitive departments and the improvement of school content have gradually achieved results. Limiting liberal arts and focusing on practical subjects have yielded obvious results. According to statistics released by the Ministry of Education, the number of graduates in practical subjects has increased by 3%, and the number of graduates in liberal arts has decreased by 3%. Freshmen in practical subjects accounted for 45% last year and jumped to 51% this year. In the past, there were more liberal arts students than practical subjects, but now practical subjects exceed liberal arts. The great effect can be seen. The amount of subsidies for private colleges and universities is also mostly used in practical subjects, and private schools benefit a lot. Students studying abroad at public expense are overwhelmingly in practical subjects. In addition to continuing the original policy, the development of higher education in the border areas is gradually being planned, such as the preparation for the establishment of National Northwest University and the subsidies for Guangxi and Yunnan Universities, which are clear examples. In addition, there is also the issue of paying attention to the career paths of university graduates. Last year, an Academic Work Advisory Office was established jointly with the National Economic Commission, and this year, a University Graduate Employment Training Class has been organized. The trend of higher education administration, in terms of nature, has gradually shifted from quantitative expansion to qualitative improvement; in terms of content, it has gradually shifted from distorted development to rational enrichment; in terms of region, it has gradually shifted from the development of cities and inland areas to the development of border areas; in terms of effectiveness, it has gradually shifted from talent cultivation to talent utilization.

In terms of general education, the major reforms in recent years have been the separation of secondary schools and normal schools, the grouping of secondary school curricula, and the active expansion of vocational education and compulsory education. In the past, secondary schools and normal schools were a mixed system, with normal departments established in senior high schools. However, due to the mixed establishment of secondary schools and normal schools, there were more disadvantages than advantages, so there was a provision for separate establishment. At present, it cannot be handled by private individuals to avoid abuses. Recently, the Ministry of Education has also established a special department in the administration to handle normal education matters. The senior high school curriculum originally had no grouping requirements, but since the implementation of the curriculum standards, the need for grouping has gradually been felt, and opinions from all parties have also expressed agreement. Therefore, there was the amendment of the secondary school curriculum standards this year, with senior high schools divided into Group A and Group B. Although there is no formal name for liberal arts and science, in reality, there is no difference between the two, and vocational subjects are set up for students to choose. The Ministry of Education has long established a department specializing in vocational education, and its importance can be seen. The vocational education funding in various provinces and cities has gradually reached the standards set by the ministry. This year, there is also a subsidy for excellent vocational schools to encourage them. Compulsory education in our country has been advocated for more than twenty years, but it has not been fully realized due to financial reasons. Until last year, through the greatest efforts of the Ministry of Education, this item of funding was included in the national budget, which is one of the most memorable events in educational administration. The budget for the 25th year has increased from 3.2 million yuan to 4.7 million yuan. In addition to establishing a Compulsory Education Committee to specialize in design, the Ministry of Education has recently added a Compulsory Education Section to manage compulsory education administrative matters. The promotion of compulsory education in the border areas has also gradually been given more attention in recent years, and the funding for border education has also increased this year. The recent establishment of a national normal school in Suiyuan is a precursor to promoting compulsory education in Mongolia and Tibet. The trend of general education administration, in terms of secondary schools, has tended towards grouping; vocational education has gradually become widespread; and compulsory education has gradually expanded from urban and rural areas to border areas.

In terms of social education, in addition to expanding public schools and public education centers, the new important facility is the implementation of broadcasting education. Broadcasting education is still a pioneering undertaking in our country. Its effectiveness is difficult to accurately assess as it has not been implemented for long. Public education has never had implementation standards. Since the Ministry of Education promulgated the regulations for public schools, curriculum facilities have had uniform standards. Recently, the Ministry of Education is working hard to edit public readings and textbooks for public schools, which are expected to be promulgated soon. The trend of social education administration has shifted from quantitative progress to substantive attention and has gradually shifted from narrow social education to broad social education.
