Municipal Education Bureau Continues to Hold the Tenth Elementary School Teacher Registration; Report and Registration Start on the 27th; Registration Method and Registration Instructions Announced

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau announced that, in order to carefully select elementary school teachers, the bureau held the ninth elementary school teacher registration last August to prepare for school appointments. Now that the academic year is beginning, schools should appoint teachers separately, so the tenth elementary school teacher registration will be continued. All those who have the qualifications prescribed in the Provisional Regulations for Elementary School Teacher Registration and are willing to serve as elementary school teachers in this city but have not passed the eighth and ninth registrations should fill out two registration forms at the bureau in person within the specified time from 9:00 AM to 11:30 AM and from 1:00 PM to 3:00 PM from July 27th (Monday) to July 30th (Thursday), with graduation certificates, service certificates, and verification certificates, and bring three recent 2.5-inch photos and their personal seal. Fill out two registration forms, a physical examination and oral examination form, together with various certificates and request registration. Oral examination will be held at Municipal Wanzhu Elementary School, Jiu Mu Di, from 8:00 AM on July 31st (Friday), and physical examination will be held at the Public Sports Field, Daji Road, Nanshi, from 9:00 AM on August 1st (Saturday). (Those who passed the fifth elementary school teacher's exemption from examination and verification but failed to comply with the physical examination due to unavoidable reasons can undergo a supplementary examination after 2:00 PM on this day.) All provisional regulations for registration and registration instructions are announced below for everyone's information.

Registration Method

Article 1: In order to select excellent teachers and improve the teaching efficiency of municipal elementary schools, the Bureau will hold a registration of elementary school teachers. All those who are willing to serve as elementary school teachers in this city should apply to the Bureau for registration in accordance with these regulations. Article 2: Those who have one of the following qualifications are allowed to register: 1. Graduates of the Department of Education of Teachers' University and University Teachers' College; 2. Graduates of Higher Normal School or Specialized Normal School; 3. Graduates of the old system Normal School, Wood Department, or Senior Middle School Normal Department or Special Normal Department; 4. Those who have one of the qualifications listed in Article 78 of the Elementary School Regulations and have passed the Elementary School Teacher Exemption from Examination and Verification and have not exceeded the prescribed time limit; 5. Those who have one of the qualifications listed in Article 79 of the Elementary School Regulations and have passed the Elementary School Teacher Examination and Verification and have not exceeded the prescribed time limit. Article 3: Those who register in accordance with the qualifications in Articles 1, 2, and 3 of Article 2 of this Regulation and pass the registration shall be allowed to serve as class teachers or specialized teachers in elementary schools in this city. Article 4: Those who register in accordance with the qualifications in Articles 4 and 5 of Article 2 of this Regulation and pass the registration shall be allowed to serve as any teacher as determined by the qualified examiner. The valid time of the registration shall be until the end of the valid time of the verification. Article 5: If a registered teacher has served in a non-educational institution or an institution unrelated to his major for more than two years, his registration shall be invalid. Article 6: Two elementary school teacher registration forms must be filled out at the time of registration, each with a recent 2.5-inch photo of the applicant, plus one additional photo (three photos in total). Article 7: At the time of registration, the graduation certificate, verification certificate, service certificate, etc. should be submitted for inspection and returned after the registration is announced. Article 8: When necessary, the Director or the Section Chief designated by the Director may summon elementary school teachers who apply for registration to hold oral or other examinations. Article 9: Those who pass the registration will be issued a registration form, and those who do not pass the registration will not be issued a registration form.

Registration Instructions

Anyone who meets one of the qualifications in Article 2 of the Provisional Regulations for Elementary School Teacher Registration of this Bureau may apply for registration. 2. The Elementary School Teacher Registration Form can be obtained from the Bureau's Information Office after signing in, limited to one copy per person (two copies). At the same time, obtain the Registration Instructions and Oral Examination Physical Examination Form. 3. Two copies of the Elementary School Teacher Registration Form should be filled out. When filling out the form, be sure to read each item carefully before filling out each item, so as not to omit anything and cause problems during review. 4. The registration form should be filled out in black or blue ink, not in pencil. The handwriting should be neat and not sloppy. 5. When registering, prepare three 2.5-inch photos (small 2-inch photos are not suitable), two photos should be affixed to the registration form, and one photo should be affixed to the back of the oral examination and physical examination form. 6. The front of the oral examination and physical examination form must be filled in with the applicant's name (no words or numbers), gender, and age. 7. When registering, submit the registration form in two copies, the oral examination and physical examination form in one copy, and various certificates such as graduation certificates and service certificates for verification at the same time, and obtain a registration receipt. 8. The registration receipt should be kept properly. The receipt will be used as proof for oral examination and physical examination and for returning documents in the future. 9. Those who have passed the fifth elementary school teacher's exemption from examination and have undergone a physical examination only need to take the oral examination. Those whose qualifications meet the requirements but have not undergone a physical examination must take the oral examination and a supplementary physical examination. Those who register directly must take the oral examination and a physical examination. 10. The date and location of the oral examination and physical examination will be determined by the Bureau and announced in the Shen and Xin newspapers. No supplementary procedures will be handled after the deadline. 11. Those who do not comply with the procedures and do not follow the regulations will not be accepted. 12. Those who have passed the eighth and ninth elementary school teacher registration do not need to re-register.

Jiangsu Provincial Government Abolishes Education Fee Audit Committees in Various Counties: Simplification of Regulations Announced by the Education Department

The Jiangsu Provincial Government, in view of the previous regulations on the preliminary audit of the income and expenditure of education funds in various counties, originally formed an audit committee composed of representatives from local party and government and education agencies to hold monthly meetings to review and prevent abuses such as omissions in receipts, excessive expenditures, and forged documents. Since its implementation, only a few have been able to conduct audits in earnest, and most have been perfunctory. Even worse, they have used the opportunity of absence and quorum to achieve their factional or personal purposes. The calculation of income and expenditure, due to the lack of a quorum, cannot be sent to the province for audit, and the number of such cases is increasing day by day, causing more abuses and failing to account for the situation. At present, each county has an accounting director to handle the preliminary audit of the income and expenditure of all public funds in the county. This County Education Fund Audit Committee should be abolished. Yesterday, a special order was issued to all counties to abolish the County Education Fund Audit Committee Regulations previously announced by the Education Department.

Suzhou Art College Engages Chang Shuhong as Professor

Since its establishment, Suzhou Art College has achieved remarkable results. It was the first to be approved by the Ministry of Education. Since the autumn of the 23rd year, the Ministry of Education has subsidized more than 10,000 yuan for equipment and has worked hard to enrich its content. In the 25th year, the Ministry of Education approved a subsidy of 6,000 yuan for the purpose of adding two teaching positions. Yan Wenliang, the president of the school, has telegraphed to Chang Shuhong, a famous artist studying in Germany, to appoint him as a professor of Western painting and design. It is also heard that Mr. Chang has replied and accepted, and will set off to return to China soon. Chang Shuhong is from Hangzhou and was a professor at the College of Engineering and Agriculture of Zhejiang University. He then went to France to study for seven years and graduated first in his class from the Lyon National School of Fine Arts. He also passed the first-place award from the Paris National Higher School of Fine Arts and was selected as a member of the Lyon Salon Super Selection Committee. The pieces he decided to produce have all won medals and honorary awards. Four of Mr. Chang's works have been purchased by the French government, and one has been purchased by the Lyon municipal government. They are now displayed in the Paris National Museum of Foreign Writers and Artists and the Lyon National Museum of Art. Mr. Chang is indeed an outstanding figure in the Chinese community studying in France in recent years.

The guild's listed price for No. 24 coarse granulated white sugar spot goods was 22 yuan, and for transit goods, it was 6 yuan and 7 cents, with continuous transactions. East White spot goods: No. 4 was 21 yuan and 9 cents, No. 8 was 21 yuan and 4 cents, and No. 9 was 21 yuan, 1 cent and 5 mills. Transit goods: No. 4 (J mark) was 6 yuan and 7 cents, No. 8 (TK mark) was 6 yuan and 5 cents and 5 mills, and TM mark was 6 yuan and 4 cents. No. 1 refined white sugar from local factories such as Zhenji, Dahua, and Jinxin were all 20 yuan and 5 cents. Several Guangchao merchants offered more than 500 bags of Hainan raw sugar at 12 yuan and 5 cents, an increase of 2 cents. A batch of 85 bags of Chongti Qing sugar was priced at 11 yuan and 6 cents. It is estimated that there were 300 bags of refined raw sugar. Jiyuan Yu was priced at 15 yuan and 1 cent, and Hechang Dexing was priced at 14 yuan and 3 cents to 1 cent, an increase of 1 to 2 cents. It is heard that Shantou exchange rates have slightly improved to 1,180 yuan, an increase of 20 yuan compared to the previous day. Only about 400 bags of Hainan raw sugar were imported from Zhou, and transactions were close to 13 yuan. The arrival of refined raw sugar is also scarce, with more than 300 bags transported from Yunnan.

Hardware: Thick Iron Spot Goods Are About to Run Out

Since the military factories, toy factories, and machine factories started purchasing thick iron, it has been selling very well. Recently, due to a sudden large-scale purchase by certain organizations, the circulating goods on the market are almost exhausted. The standard price has therefore risen steadily. Currently, the market price for No. 24 (30-inch, 36-inch) is 140 yuan per box, which is 5 yuan higher than before. No. 26 (30-inch, 36-inch) is 90 yuan per box, which is also 7 to 8 yuan higher than before. A type of "wild chicken" goods (70 sheets per box, weighing 200 pounds) is priced at 70 yuan. Because of the shortage of genuine goods, customers and factories are buying as much as possible. It is reported that more than 100 boxes were offered on the market yesterday, so the market is expected to continue to be bullish.

Dried and Preserved Goods: Zhangzhou Twigs Prices Fall Frequently; First Batch of Four Pieces of Hainan Longan Arrive

Yesterday, the price of Zhangzhou twigs kept falling because the market price of sorted Lan Zhu goods was cheaper than before, and the production price telegraph reported a drop later. Therefore, by the afternoon, when the merchants opened the market, the market was sluggish, and the price of ordinary goods fell by a small amount of three or four yuan. The price reduction of the remaining black leaf twigs was not significant because of the small arrival volume. If sales are smooth in the future, there is hope for a recovery, otherwise it will be difficult to stabilize.

It is heard that the first batch of new Hainan longan, four pieces, has been delivered to the merchants yesterday. The samples have not been seen yet, and the market is expected to open around today or tomorrow.

Shen Bao Literary Supplement

Her Frustration

— Long Gonggong

I have seen a failed philanthropist. This setback seemed to have confused her with irreparable blows, and finally plunged her into inexplicable sorrow. She was called Second Granny Zhou. She lived in a side street of Ren Zhonghua Middle Road (a market in Guangzhou famous for buying and selling used clothes, just like Shilu or Wusong Road in Shanghai). She was fat, and her attire from the ear pick on her head to the cloth shoes on her feet was very old-fashioned. Her purpose in doing good deeds was not to help others, but to help her own existing or future children and grandchildren.

One afternoon, thirty or forty beggars came to Zhonghua Middle Road. They were all from the local area and nearby villages. No one knew how they gathered together and ran there. Their clothes - more accurately, some tattered sacks and pieces of cloth - had lost their original meaning as clothes and had become randomly arranged decorations on their bodies, revealing various parts of their bodies: bones, sparse body hair, sores, rotten tumors, and reproductive organs like horses and wild dogs.

It was winter, and they sat under a white wall full of sunshine like a tired team of long-distance walkers all made up of men, laughing loudly, sighing, singing, and cursing. The constable was a young man with an eye disease. He borrowed the telephone from a business to report the incident to the police station. Then he stood next to the pile of beggars, holding his eyes with a handkerchief, pretending not to care about them at all. What was the police station's solution? - Someone asked him, but he just shook his head, indicating that he was unwilling to say. Therefore, I guess it might be the kind of order that is difficult to execute:

"You bastard! Are they going to sit in your post forever? - Pay attention to when they leave, or you find a way to drive them away..."

Second Granny Zhou ran over with a bamboo basket. Her anxious and pitiful appearance was as if she was carrying a brass-nozzled canvas hose to a fire scene, walking without choosing her way. Even in such a heroic occasion, her fat limbs still stumbled like a mother goose. She spoke loudly to the shop assistants on both sides of the sidewalk. Every time the features on her face squeezed, it made people see the oil oozing from every pore. The bamboo basket contained a roll of ten dollars worth of small change - that was fifty double dimes. In Guangzhou, people are used to rolling ten dollars into a roll as thick as a chicken neck. Second Granny Zhou broke open the silver dimes in front of the beggars, ordered those strangely shaped men to stand still and not move, and then distributed her alms to them one by one according to the number of people.

The silver coins made a crisp sound when they were shaken and grabbed - this sound subdued those despised and lowly creatures, and they immediately became orderly and good citizens. Second Granny Zhou walked among them with extraordinary joy, speaking in a voice as if she were singing sweet song lines.

"You there, you one there!

You there, you another one there!"

But when it came to the seventeenth person, she was deceived, lost her dignity, joy, and harmony.

"You cheap bone! You 'buried on the mountainside'! I recognize you, you just took two dimes from me, why are you here again?"

She scolded the beggar. And from among that pile of waste-like men, someone shouted at the same time:

"What about him? What about him? Qi Toulin also got a second share!" Qi Toulin

(This is a nickname with insulting meaning) and the person who shouted started fighting each other first.

Second Granny Zhou's sacred and happy feelings were shattered, as if she had been bitten by a dog while feeding it. She raised her hand and hit the seventeenth beggar. She punished the evildoer without thinking because his greedy heart had ruined all this purity.

The beggars began to snatch the silver dimes, bumping into each other fiercely, twisting together, forming a large chaotic conflict. Some people threw the dimes far away, and everyone chased after them. Some crawled horizontally on the ground, one pressing on top of the other. Some continued to bump into each other unexpectedly but frequently, and fell down.

Second Granny Zhou lost everything and was then pulled out of the crowd by the constable with the eye disease. She stood next to the people fighting in the melee that she had caused, which no one could calm down, stomping her feet and scolding. The shop assistants on both sides of the sidewalk laughed loudly at this uncontrollable scene...

Jia Tangguan

— Yin Guang

This is a very healthy old man, with a sharp and snow-white beard, and a face as full and shiny as a child's, only covered with wrinkles, yellow with black, looking like cultivated Coptis chinensis. No matter how two or three young people who consider themselves humorous cannot help but smirk and purse their lips when they see him walk into the teahouse. In fact, he is still considered a very reputable person in the county town. He has been a public servant in the county for fifteen or sixteen years, but in terms of fame, he is only a student of the Imperial Academy. When investigating his background, he is not an important figure's "old cousin's old cousin." Just from this point, we can know how unreasonable it is to despise him.

This may be what is called good luck in old age. He lived silently until he was nearly sixty years old before he began to appear on the county's political stage, and it was so sudden that even he himself could hardly believe it. At that time, the one in power in the whole county was Chen Sandai Wu, a cunning and venomous man. His great-grandfather was a tribute student, he himself had stayed in a government-run law school for a few days, and his brother was a famous leader of the former Old Society. With these forces, one autumn, he finally defeated his political enemy, a madman with the title of "Ju Ren" (a degree attained in the imperial examinations). Thus, the old man began his political career.

Originally, as soon as Sandai Wu came to power, several key figures in the various organs, some of whom considered themselves noble, and some of whom had too close a relationship with the madman with the title of "Ju Ren," unanimously adopted a policy of non-cooperation and resigned one after another. He was in a dilemma because he was wary of some of the successors, and some of them were wary of him. But one morning, as he was squatting on a wicker chair smoking a water pipe, feeling frustrated, he suddenly slapped his forehead and laughed to himself, "How could I forget Jia Tangguan!" Thus, from this time until his death, the old man rarely wavered in his position as chairman of the Farmers' Association, as if it were a lifelong position.

He was very amiable and always smiled, with intelligent and gentle eyes. He could talk to anyone, and although he didn't say much, he wouldn't give you a headache. Anger and impatience were not related to him. The characteristic of his entire character seemed to be only his peace and openness. He had a son, who was very handsome and had stayed in a military academy for three months, but he died when the old man turned sixty. Even this did not agitate him much. Half a year later, he calmly took in a maid as his concubine, saying, "This is more convenient."

After this incident, whenever people talked about how he could be as healthy as a middle-aged man, he would laugh heartily, tap the tip of his beard with his finger, and then answer seriously, "Didn't the book say it? 'Xiao, bu zhi zai?' (Small, is it not a supplement?)". His smile would immediately fill his face again.

His family was not wealthy, only having two or three shi of unpolished rice sent by tenant farmers every year. The house was rented, but he lived comfortably, without any extravagant desires. He was even more unwilling to touch any unclean money. It was precisely because of this that he had never been a witness in several cases of financial corruption in the county town's public affairs. The only thing he thought he shouldn't let go of was his regular salary. Because it was somewhat of a mandatory nature, the salary was very small, and it was often in arrears. But even if he came back empty-handed from the local revenue and expenditure office for three months in a row, he would not be disappointed. He could calmly wait for an opportunity: when the heads of those local agencies initiated an official document asking him to stamp it, he only needed to roll his eyes and talk to them about the weather, and that would be enough. Originally, according to the old man's habit, as soon as he saw the sealed envelope, he would unhesitatingly pull out his Shoushan stone personal seal. Even some people who did not know his temperament, for the sake of name and responsibility, insisted that he look at the contents of the official document, but he would refuse.

"I won't look," he said with a smile, shaking his head, "I'll just stamp it for you." So he casually stamped his seal under his title.

If someone else made such a simple move, it would definitely cause discomfort to the opposing party, but it rarely happened to him. Because there could be such a person in the world, who is usually difficult to speak up, always silent, showing a friendly appearance, but when they unexpectedly say every word clearly, you will blush in the first minute, feeling that there are bones in those words. But when you carefully examine their intelligent and frank eyes, you will naturally breathe a sigh of relief and smile along with him. The old man was exactly this kind of character.

Moreover, in some occasions, his out-of-the-blue remarks, which made inexperienced people embarrassed, could also lead to some unexpected practical effects, which not only made people feel interesting. Once, at a county administrative meeting, in order to impose additional land taxes, two equally matched political leaders suddenly slammed the table and argued, and even the partisans on both sides were ready to fight. At this time, the old man calmly touched the teacup with his finger and said with a smile, "What are you arguing about? It will be passed anyway!" Everyone frowned immediately, but then they couldn't help but laugh.

He attended the county administrative meetings every time, although he rarely expressed his opinions. He always sat next to the county magistrate, silently drinking tea, sometimes looking at the participants who were stating their opinions in a high-pitched voice, and then immediately staring at his own teacup and smiling, as if he was there to listen in, or as a token gesture. However, whenever a proposal was put to a vote, he would not forget to raise his hand, and he had never not raised his hand to agree. Although he seemed like the representatives from those remote small towns who came to the meeting, he often did not understand the content of the proposals they were voting on. The difference was that those honest and timid local gentry would always pat others on the shoulder after the meeting and ask, "Hey, what was passed just now?" And when they raised their hands, they would also look at the other participants. If there were too few people raising their hands to agree, or if the people they considered important were still blowing their water pipes noisily, they would blush and reluctantly drag their arms down. But the old man was not like this. As long as he expressed his approval, it was as if everything was over.

He also rarely missed other gatherings, such as welcoming newly appointed officials; especially various banquets. At every banquet, he always sat in the seat of honor, and as soon as he sat down at the table, he would always remember to pull out a faded white handkerchief from his arms with a smile, muttering to himself, "Let me take some back for my grandson." Then he would leisurely reach his hands into the plates and dishes of fruits and various preserved meats.

He passed away five years ago. His death caused great inconvenience to several important figures. Whenever they were troubled by the selection of personnel for various agencies and organizations, they would always remember him and say angrily, "Damn it! It would have been better if Jia Tangguan hadn't died!"

Lighthearted Burden

— TK

Rainy Day Poem

— Chu Yang

My mood these days I can't even be sure of myself

Like a misty lake on a rainy day:

The weather is uncertain, and dark clouds often shroud the sun;

The bright sail shadow is gone,

And it is difficult to distinguish the white gulls that are rippling on the edge of the water bottom.

Imagination, oh, that is a distant, unknown village!

Dream, oh, do you want to find grapes in thorns?

The lilies in the wilderness are all dead.

It is all poppies, blooming with purple and yellow poisonous flowers.

Do you want to suck the intoxicating fragrance of anesthesia with your dry mouth?

This heavy rain cannot wash away my mood,

Just as a torrent of tears cannot exhaust my sorrow.

Raindrops hit the lake surface, stirring up countless ripples,

My mood can never be calm.

Oh, the scene after the storm is too terrible

That deathly silence is too terrible!

Let my heartstrings beat forever without stopping,

Let the vitality of youth not be extinguished so early.

This rainy day is so lovely:

The wheat is yellow, the seedlings are green

The universe is always creating.

Put down the "departure" in your arms, pick up the hoe,

The land of life needs you to work hard,

Isn't a great sunny day after the continuous rain!

Soviet Communications

Gorky's Funeral

— Ge Baoquan

June 18th in the Soviet Union was a day of rest (note), but also a very unfortunate day. It was on this day, at 11:10 in the morning, that the great Soviet writer Maxim Gorky passed away due to a long illness at his villa near Moscow. After the Central Committee of the Soviet Union and the People's Committee announced this unfortunate news, Moscow became a city of sorrow. Black-bordered mourning flags on a red background were hung everywhere along the streets. Bookstore windows displayed Gorky's works, portraits, and bronze statues. Theaters canceled their performances, and cultural and recreational parks were temporarily closed, all expressing widespread grief over the death of this great writer.

By the morning of the 19th, newspapers were printed with large characters announcing the news of Gorky's death, along with condolences from Romain Rolland, George Bernard Shaw, and H.G. Wells, as well as mourning and commemorative texts written by Lenin's widow, André Gide, and other Soviet writers. For example, an editorial in *Pravda* stated that Gorky's death was like "the extinguishing of a lamp of reason." The editorial concluded, "Great is Gorky's genius, great is his service to the new humanity; his shining name will never be submerged by the flowing waters of the Lethe—the river of forgetfulness. The name of this great Russian writer, the brilliant artist of words, the close friend of laborers, and the warrior who fought for the victory of building a new society, will forever shine like the sun and stars, remaining in human memory, lasting for thousands of years!" Romain Rolland's condolence message was very short, just a few lines: "Regarding the death of our dear friend, I truly cannot describe how saddened I am. We now equally share the sorrow of the Soviet people." George Bernard Shaw said, "With him, the writers of the nineteenth century, his contemporaries, have become weaker by one." A commemorative text written by the Soviet writer Alexei Tolstoy included these words: "The light of the era of the three great revolutions has dimmed, and the last great writer of Russia has left us. Thanks to his art, the best traditions of pre-revolutionary literature, its most noble humanitarian ideals, and its ability to love, feel, and understand the human soul, can be connected to the still-young Soviet literature. He was our—strict and uncompromising—leader. From an artistic standpoint, he demanded even greater service. He was also the founder of Soviet humanism."

Gorky passed away in the village of Gorky, not far from Moscow. His body was transported to Moscow that day for a state funeral. The Soviet government also organized a national funeral committee to handle all funeral matters. From 9:00 AM on the 19th, Gorky's body was first laid in state in the Hall of Columns of the House of Trade Unions, where people could go to pay their respects. On that day, Gorky's portrait and four large mourning flags were hung in front of the House of Trade Unions. Gorky's body lay in the center of the Hall of Columns, surrounded by flowers and wreaths. An orchestra played funeral marches by Beethoven, Chopin, and Grieg. Government officials, famous writers, and representatives from various places stood beside the body as the Guard of Honor. For example, Stalin, Molotov, Orjonikidze, and Andreyea went to pay their respects at 4:30 PM that afternoon and stood beside the body for several minutes. On that day, Moscow's radio station also stopped broadcasting various programs, and all that could be heard were mournful music and mourning poems and prose discussed by Soviet writers. From eight or nine o'clock in the morning, crowds lined up to go to the House of Trade Unions, hoping to catch a last glimpse of Gorky's face. By that afternoon, the crowds had grown even larger. Gorky Street, Bolshaya Dmitrovka Street, and Petrovka Street, near the House of Trade Unions, were temporarily closed to traffic. The queue stretched for several miles. It is estimated that over one to two hundred thousand people passed before Gorky's body that day, which shows how much the Soviet people respected Gorky.

Gorky's body was cremated that night, and the ashes were placed in a small copper urn. From 9:00 AM on the 20th, it was still laid in state in the Hall of Columns of the House of Trade Unions, where people could go to pay their respects until the funeral. The funeral was held in Red Square in the center of Moscow. Red Square was very close to the House of Trade Unions. The route was lined with soldiers, police, and crowds. Only those with passes could go to Red Square to participate in the funeral. At 5:30, the funeral began. Stalin, Molotov, Kaganovich, and Orjonikidze stood beside Gorky's ashes as the final Guard of Honor. Then, to the sound of the Internationale, the small pavilion housing the urn was carried to Red Square. In front of the pavilion, someone held Gorky's portrait and a small red pillow with a Soviet government award, the Order of Lenin, on it. Behind the pavilion were Gorky's family, government officials, and writers.

As the funeral procession proceeded to Red Square, military bands played funeral marches along the way. Upon arriving at Red Square, the small pavilion housing the urn was placed on a red cloth-covered table in front of Lenin's Mausoleum. Stalin and others then walked up to Lenin's Mausoleum to begin the memorial ceremony. Molotov first gave a speech on behalf of the government and the Central Executive Committee of the Party. In his speech, Molotov said, "Since Lenin, Gorky's death is truly a great loss for the Soviet Union and all of humanity." Then, Bulganin gave a speech on behalf of the Moscow Soviet and the Moscow Provincial Party Committee, Alexei Tolstoy gave a speech on behalf of the Soviet Writers' Union, and finally, André Gide gave a speech in French. Gide said, "Gorky's death is not only a misfortune for the Soviet Union but for the entire world. Because of Gorky, the painful and great voice of the Russian people found an echo in countries near and far. Therefore, what I want to express here is not only my personal sorrow but the sorrow of the French literary world, the sorrow of the entire European cultural world, and the sorrow of the entire world cultural world." Finally, Gide said, "The greatest and most glorious task that Gorky bore throughout his life was to connect the old and new worlds and to build a bridge between the new world and the world of the future. He witnessed all the oppression and tragic struggles of the past, and he used his strength to help bring about today's victory. He spoke on behalf of the many who could not express their opinions, making their voices heard far and wide. From now on, Gorky is a historical figure and one of the great figures of all time."

After the speeches, Stalin and Tolstoy carried the pavilion with the ashes, passing to the right of Lenin's Mausoleum, and to the Kremlin wall behind the tomb. All the Soviet revolutionaries and government officials, as well as foreign revolutionary fighters who died in Moscow, were buried here. Gorky's ashes were placed in the wall to the sound of the Internationale and a 21-gun salute. Now, there is a black plaque on the wall that reads: "Alexei Maximovich Gorky. Born on March 28, 1868, Died on June 18, 1936."

At the time of Gorky's death, it is worth briefly discussing Gorky's life. Gorky's original name was Alexei Maximovich Peshkov, born on March 28, 1868, in Nizhny Novgorod (now Gorky City). Maxim Gorky was the pen name he later used for his works. His father was a carpenter, and his mother was the daughter of a dyer. Both died when Gorky was young, so Gorky spent most of his childhood living with his grandparents. At the age of eight, he attended primary school, but the school's curriculum did not spark his interest. Coupled with his family's poverty, he dropped out after a year or two and was sent to work as an apprentice in a shoemaker's shop. Details of his life at his grandparents' home and during his schooling can be found in his autobiographical novel, "My Childhood."

From the age of twelve, Gorky began a wandering life. He first worked as a dishwasher on a Volga River steamboat. At this time, there was a cook on the ship who often asked Gorky to read novels to him. According to Gorky himself, this was the first person to spark his love for literature. After leaving the steamboat, he also worked as an apprentice in an icon shop and as a small supervisor in a construction factory. In his spare time, he continued to read literary books. At the age of sixteen, he went to Kazan, hoping to study at the local university. However, this beautiful dream ultimately fell through, and he continued to live a wandering life, working as a porter at the dock and as an apprentice in a bakery. During this period, Gorky associated with progressive intellectuals and people engaged in revolutionary work. At the same time, he personally experienced the lives of various lower-class social groups. Therefore, Gorky said, this was his education, this was his "university."

In 1891, Gorky wandered to Tiflis in the Caucasus. In September of the following year, he published his first debut work in the Caucasus newspaper (Kavkaz). This can be said to be the beginning of his literary life. At the end of the same year, he returned to his hometown, where he was promoted and helped by the writer Korolenko. He formally embarked on a literary career and gradually gained fame in the literary world. From this time on, in addition to writing, Gorky also participated in the revolutionary movement. He was arrested and exiled several times. Even when he later went into exile abroad, he continued to engage in revolutionary work and became one of Lenin's close friends. In 1932, the Soviet government held a grand commemorative meeting to celebrate the fortieth anniversary of Gorky's literary career.

Gorky's works include the novels "My Childhood," "My Universities," "Mother," and "The Life of Klim Samgin." "The Life of Klim Samgin" has been published in three volumes, and the fourth volume was completed just before his death. His plays include "The Petty Bourgeois," "The Lower Depths," "Enemies," "Yegor Bulychov and Others," and others.

After Gorky's death, his brain was handed over to the Brain Research Institute in Moscow for anatomical research. His manuscripts are being edited and published by the Gorky Manuscripts Committee organized by the government. Statues of Gorky are planned to be erected in the three cities of Moscow, Leningrad, and Gorky. The State Literary Publishing House of Leningrad has established a Gorky Literary Prize to encourage Soviet writers to engage in writing. Regarding Gorky's works, 800,000 copies had been sold before the Great Revolution. From the beginning of the Great Revolution until recently, there have been a total of 150 versions in various national languages, and 387 versions in Russian, with a total sales volume of more than 31 million copies. Currently, various publishing houses in the Soviet Union are also planning to publish large quantities of new complete works and various popular versions. From this, it can be seen how widespread Gorky's works are and how common they are to read. Now that Gorky has passed away, recalling his life, how he went from being a vagrant to becoming a world-famous writer, his spirit of hard work and struggle is truly worthy of our admiration. As for his works, they will also be immortal and become one of the important milestones in the history of world literature.

(Note) The Soviet Union adopted a six-day week system, meaning six workdays and one day of rest. The 6th, 12th, 18th, 24th, and 30th of each month are rest days.

Gorky's body laid in state in the Hall of Columns of the House of Trade Unions, where people could go to pay their respects.

Supplement of the Shanghai Daily

Talking Points

Fly Death Case at the University

— Me

Li Gan from Zhejiang and He Cangyun from Guangdong were students at St. John's University. On the 15th of this month, Li Gan bought a plate of egg fried rice from the kitchen. After eating only half of it, Li suddenly found a fly in the rice. He negotiated with the kitchen staff, at which time Zheng Jinhai, the kitchen bookkeeper, was calculating accounts with Zhang Yuanquan, the kitchen owner. There were large and small legal tender bills on the table. Li took one yuan of legal tender, saying it was temporarily a deposit. Later, Zhang Yuanquan asked Li to return the one yuan, leading to an argument. Zhang accused Li of being a robber, stealing five silver dollars, which angered Li. He Cangyun stepped forward and punched Zhang hard in the neck, causing Zhang to fall to the ground injured. He was sent to the hospital for treatment but died. The case was handed over to the criminal court of the First Special Court for trial the other day. He and Li are still denying the punch. The facts of the case were disclosed in the newspaper as such. Since the case is being tried by the court, the true facts will be investigated by the court. The students will be held responsible for whatever criminal charges they face, and the court will make a judgment. I don't need to elaborate. What I want to talk about is the issue of students' personal cultivation.

Let's assume that the facts are true for now. The first cause of the death was that the kitchen did not pay attention to hygiene, resulting in a fly being found in the egg fried rice. The kitchen is also responsible for neglecting its duties. The second cause was that the student seized one yuan of legal tender, and the subsequent request for its return led to the current tragedy. Therefore, the first fault lies with the kitchen, and the second fault lies with the student. Most kitchen staff in schools are careless and few pay attention to hygiene and cleanliness. Therefore, similar incidents involving flies are not uncommon in schools. The student should have reported the matter to the school authorities and had the kitchen punished to prevent similar incidents from happening in the future. That would have been the end of the matter.

The tragedy occurred because of the seizure of one yuan of legal tender. This kind of behavior is clearly wrong in terms of the student's character. It is clear that the student's seizure of one yuan was not to steal the money but was a kind of playful act. If it was said that the one yuan was a deposit, is the student's life only worth one yuan? If it was to steal the money, why did the student only take one yuan and stop there? In short, the student's act of seizing one yuan as a deposit not only unexpectedly led to a tragedy, which was not foreseen, but also damaged the student's character.

Therefore, I learned a lesson from the student's actions this time. Students are full of youthful energy and rely on their strength to act fiercely. They often act impulsively and are unwilling to consider things carefully. Once a punch is thrown, life is lost. By this point, it is too late to stop. The cause was only a fly, and the seizure was only one yuan of legal tender, yet it led to such an unfortunate result. How could the student have foreseen this? Students have no deep-seated hatred for the kitchen, and there is no reason to deliberately cause death. Yet, unknowingly, they "created a huge disaster." Young people must not be reckless when doing things. This is a clear example.

Singing Girl Liu Chun

— Liu Ziming

The sun was already high overhead, but Liu Chun's room was still quiet without a sound. Her mother, Zeng Jue, walked back and forth at the door, but afraid of disturbing her daughter's sweet dreams, she would only peek in and then walk away upon seeing the curtains drawn.

Liu Chun was a singing girl at the Flying Immortal Pavilion. Because she was beautiful and knew how to handle customers, the money-spending gentlemen and young masters were so happy that Liu Chun became the red singing girl at the Flying Immortal Pavilion. Every day she went on stage, the placards with requests for her songs were hung up one after another. She often sang until her voice was hoarse. Although the customers didn't care about her singing, her companions became jealous and deliberately spoke ill of her backstage to mock her. On stage, Liu Chun received applause and cheers from the customers, but backstage she was alone. She often wanted to have an opportunity to explain her difficulties to her sisters, but because she was a red singing girl, a deep divide had already been built between her and her companions. They treated her like an enemy. She could only wear a smiling face to win the customers' favor and could not get sympathy from her sisters who shared the same fate. She lived a lonely and solitary life.

It was the day before yesterday. As soon as she came off stage, the boss was already waiting backstage.

"Hard work, hard work, Miss Liu." The boss shrugged his shoulders and personally wrung a towel for Liu Chun. Of course, that was a common occurrence. The boss was always particularly attentive to his cash cow. But that day's situation seemed a little special. The boss waited until Liu Chun had removed her makeup and then whispered mysteriously in her ear:

"Several gentlemen have invited Miss Liu to go boating on the lake. They are waiting for you outside the door. Please do us the honor."

Liu Chun did not answer. She stared at the boss. The boss misunderstood her meaning and whispered even more modestly: "It's the table that ordered thirty plays today."

"Boss," Liu Chun almost laughed, "Don't you know the rules here? Please thank them for me. Singing girls don't have that kind of fortune!"

The boss took a step closer, chuckling. His face seemed to be reflected in a funhouse mirror, like a pug. He spoke a little louder:

"Miss Liu, you really don't know this. They are all officials, with section chiefs and ministers and all. Who would be afraid to accompany them boating?" He took another step closer, comparing heights with Liu Chun, "They don't care about spending money. Look, isn't it thirty plays at once? Miss Liu, congratulations! Hahaha..."

Without waiting for Liu Chun to answer, the boss went to the customers, still laughing, to reply to their invitation. Liu Chun seemed to have lost consciousness, hanging her head and following behind him. There were four or five people waiting outside the door. Seeing Liu Chun behind the boss, they rushed forward, shouting "Miss Liu, do us the honor!" (If you close your eyes and think about it, we can often see that kind of slapstick performance on stage.)

Summer nights are particularly short. Liu Chun arrived home just as the sky was about to turn white. She was slightly drunk, her face flushed, and her palms were clammy. She got out of the car in a daze. When her mother came to open the door, she stumbled into the old woman's arms.

The next day, Liu Chun fell ill and asked for leave from the day shift. The boss panicked and took a car to her house, bringing several kinds of Western medicine and inviting a famous doctor to diagnose her. The doctor said that she had caught a cold and would be fine after a few days of rest.

But the Flying Immortal Pavilion could not do business without Liu Chun. The day shift hung up a sign saying that Liu Chun was on sick leave. Those customers who hadn't even sat down all turned back, and many more asked whether she would be on stage for the night shift.

The boss had not left Liu Chun's room by dinnertime. He just paced in circles with his hands behind his back, as if Liu Chun would immediately jump out of bed. Seeing that it was almost time for the Flying Immortal Pavilion to open, a young shop assistant was waiting outside for news of whether Liu Chun would be on stage. The boss finally pulled Liu Chun's mother aside and talked for a long time, and then she talked to her daughter for a long time. In the last ten minutes, the boss took Liu Chun to the Flying Immortal Pavilion by car.

When she returned, Liu Chun's face was pale, her fever was getting higher and higher, and she tossed and turned in bed, unable to sleep soundly. She took the medicine and didn't fall asleep until dawn.

After lunch, the boss came again. Liu Chun's mother had no choice but to go to the room to wake her daughter. Liu Chun's fever had not subsided, her cheeks were red, and she was sweating all over. She glanced at the boss, turned over, and went back to sleep.

The boss carefully sat on the edge of the bed and reached out to feel her forehead.

"Miss Liu, don't be angry. Your own body is important. To be honest, it's all my fault, but what can I do when I'm eating this rice bowl? They are officials, how can I, ×, let her run into the Flying Immortal Pavilion? Miss Liu, I've already hung up the leave sign for the day shift. Take good care of yourself, and we'll see about tonight. The Flying Immortal Pavilion relies on Miss Liu..."

Liu Chun couldn't help but cry. Was the boss sympathizing with her? Absolutely not. The customers were playing with her, the boss was using her, and her sisters were jealous of her. She had no one who loved her, no one who sympathized with her, only beauty, youth, and the selling of her soul! She thought about the future. Could she be a singing girl all her life?

"Mom," she cried out, "I can't eat this rice bowl anymore! I can't eat this rice bowl anymore!"

Her mother, with tears streaming down her face, stroked her hot cheeks. "Child, calm down. Your body is important. Don't think wildly..." The old woman herself thought of her dead husband, her dead son. She only had this one daughter left. She hoped that her daughter would marry well, but was being a singing girl a way out?

Miscellaneous Writings from a Mountain City

— Especially

Unexpectedly, we, this group, are delayed in this mountain city.

From morning until sunset, looking at the sky, it always wears an unhappy face. It's been hard to enjoy the sunshine these past two days. The musty dampness in the inn keeps rushing into my nostrils, a mixed stench that makes you want to retch. The sun, which we disliked so much on our journey, is now something we long for, hoping it will reveal its cruel face and fiercely shine on every dark corner, so that all the hidden spirits lurking in those corners will be completely annihilated.

People accustomed to city hotels can never imagine the stifling atmosphere of a mountain inn. Low pressure extends from the front desk all the way to the backyard. Not only can you not hear the sound of mahjong and laughter, you can't even find fellow travelers staying at the inn. Loneliness envelops the entire place, with a bitterness that feels like your throat is being choked.

The distant mountain peaks, blurred like gauze mist,

Page 20

press down on the walls of the surrounding buildings. Chaos signifies the arrival of evening, and I resolutely taste the unwillingness to walk the pebbled road. Truly, there should be some gains today, right?

Usually, at dusk, in the relatively lively areas, to the left or right, you can often see several small tables arranged, draped with faded red woolen cloths. On top, there are writing brushes and inkstones, along with small offerings like incense and candles. The tabletop looks quite complicated, but you can't quite see it clearly. The area under the table is very warm, beyond people's line of sight. On one end, there's also a book placed, stacked high. The arrangement is somewhat like a fortune-telling stall in Shanghai, but you can't see anyone.

At first, strange thoughts kept stirring. Why can't you see anyone? Why are the tables propped up so high? Asking Ah Huang yields no definite answer. I thought: Maybe they are seeking divine guidance? Maybe they are writing letters and official documents for others? Maybe they are storytellers and fortune tellers? Who can say for sure? Like a riddle, it weighed on my mind for several days, unable to be solved. Today, the opportunity is quite opportune. A dozen people are gathered under the table, and a bearded elder is quoting from books and lecturing on maxims. The red flames of the candles cast light on the old man's face, revealing a remarkable degree of gauntness.

However, a traveler from afar cannot understand the local dialect. What exactly is the old man lecturing about? I cannot know, but he presents a quite solemn appearance. An idea slips into my mind: perhaps this is some kind of missionary work within a society? Here, I directly perceive the greatness of the power of preaching. At the same time, I cannot help but feel great admiration for this elaborate setup.

Late in the evening, the inn's food is too spicy to eat. I head to the large teahouse at the intersection of the T-shaped street, where dinner is not a problem. Brew a pot of tea, order a plate of large meat-filled buns, and at most, another one or two bowls of mutton noodles, enough to make you go back with a full stomach. In this way, the business is no less prosperous than any tea room in Shanghai.

In the teahouse, on the walls or pillars in places that don't obstruct the view, besides notices like "Beware of Money Loss" and "Personal Belongings at Your Own Risk," you rarely see phrases like "Do Not Discuss State Affairs." Although there are many people, the topics are mostly trivial household matters and business dealings. They seem to have completely cut off ties with national affairs. Originally, transportation hinders outside culture. In a mountain city where the level of culture cannot be raised, how can they appreciate everything outside?

The Stout Man on a Long Journey

— Zhuang Ruiyuan

In appearance and manner, because I resemble my younger brother in some ways, there have been huge misunderstandings. Apart from that, our differences are truly too great. Especially in temperament and interests, we are irreconcilable enemies.

We have always been together, but he has always been silent. No, he only shows hostility, plotting, and actions that are detrimental to me. I know my brother's temperament and interests. I have no resentment. Every time I use my fingers to smooth out the worry on my forehead, I also try to smooth out the worry on his forehead; but my efforts are all in vain, only increasing his hostility, plotting, and more actions detrimental to me.

Thus, the worlds that each of us privately construct are isolated from each other, very, very far apart. Although we have the same wounds, we have never confided in each other as a form of consolation, a form of support.

On winter nights, we silently drank some water to moisten our throats, which had become dry from the stove fire. But we would never easily break the silence between us just because we had moistened throats.

What a tiring long journey we are walking!

Only occasionally, we would sigh listlessly like this, using the same tired tone. Yes, we both clearly understand our journey, and yet we are such unfamiliar and unfortunate companions on the road! I would endure all the unbearable trembling, trying to support my younger brother as we walked our thorny path. I would have no resentment, anger, or regrets. For my brother's sake, I allowed him to question everything I did. On the lonely long journey, it should be beneficial for him to have his older brother accompanying him.

I tirelessly took care of him, comforted him, held his hand so he wouldn't leave me. Everything was for my brother's sake.

However, he, a person whose temperament and interests were opposed to mine, repaid me with hostility, plotting, and actions detrimental to me. He desperately struggled to break free of my hand. He wanted to break away from my care. He resolutely shouldered all the difficult and complex ambitions. He left me with these firm words:

"Go away! I hate you. Your companionship is just another burden to me. I want to go outside alone, to seek, suffer, and even destroy myself for my own sake. And you should also explore your own path!" Thus, my younger brother walked away from me, and further and further apart. I knew that on the long road full of dust and wind, my younger brother was still struggling, forever seeking, suffering, and even destroying himself for his own sake. On his forehead, the worry that my fingers had once smoothed out may have already disappeared. He would laugh, sing in the desert, without worry or pain!

But in me, the worry that I had once smoothed out existed again on my forehead, because I had lost my younger brother. Although we both clearly understand our journey, and yet we are such unfamiliar and unfortunate companions on the road!"

"But, come back! Brother."

In the wind and snow, in the dust storm, I lowered my face, feeling utterly exhausted. I only mumbled this outdated phrase to myself.

Drunk Sleeping on the Battlefield

Fine grape wine, luminous cup at night, urged to drink by pipa on horseback, do not laugh at my drunken sleep on the battlefield, how many have returned from ancient battles, camping in ancient temples early, lodging in desolate suburbs at night, the wind whistles, the fish murmurs, my drinking spirit is especially strong, howling to the sky, plucking the strings, drawing the sword, enemies arrive, war drums thunder, not afraid of guns, not afraid of cannons, a cry of forward march, jumping out onto the battlefield, charging to sweep away the enemies, still not fully awake from my slumber, my battle robe stained with blood, the remaining enemies have fled, I urge you to drink another cup of wine, the clouds are light, the sky is high, the stars are sparse, the moon is bright, sand as a pillow, smoke as a blanket, battlefield dream, a dream far away.

Movie

Bai Yushuang Has Never "Been Circled"

Division Commander Xu Xinyuan came to the governor's office to see Governor Tan Zhiyuan. He smelled the extraordinary aroma of the cigars the governor was smoking. He asked for one to try, but the governor said: "This was sent by the consul. It costs three yuan apiece. I can't let you smoke it." The division commander impolitely reached into the drawer and rummaged around. He found a cigarette case, opened it, and saw that it was full of women's photos, some with circles drawn on them, and some without. The division commander asked curiously, and the governor replied humorously: "The ones with circles are the ones who have been 'circled.'" The clever division commander understood the governor's words: "Hahahaha, that's not bad. Why hasn't Haitanghong (Bai Yushuang) been circled yet?" These words reminded the governor. He immediately called the chief secretary and told him to call Haitanghong, who had not yet been circled. The chief secretary repeatedly agreed and went to carry out the order. The governor proudly praised the chief secretary: "The chief secretary's methods of handling these matters are famous."

A Trivial Talk on "Going to Nature"

Due to a kind of pretentious affectation, human nature has long been diminished because of it. In the world, there may still be the existence of rich and poor classes; however, in primitive life, there is only the competition for survival, creating and enjoying by one's own strength.

From the civilized, material world, going to nature, some people will feel that man is a waste, but in the eyes of others, he can use his vitality to resist and overcome this nature.

Essentially speaking, there is no existence of rich and poor classes in the world. That is entirely an artificial affectation; what exists is only the division of intelligence.

"Going to Nature" is written with this theme. We first see people in tall buildings, mansions, brocade clothes, and delicacies; when they go to a deserted island and are completely cut off from the outside world, they cannot tolerate this original life. Because of their own incompetence, they forget the existence of class and succumb to the power of nature. But when they return to civilized society, they immediately forget the lessons of primitive life.

"Going to Nature" does not mean that people should return to nature. Even in a civilized society, this principle can be applied to make this society more natural and more humane, allowing people to obtain their due rewards based on their respective intelligence. Survival of the fittest is the law of nature.

The whole play is completely immersed in a poetic state, but this is not a utopian fantasy; this explains the axiom of natural selection - what kind of existence is mankind.

Hu Ping Was Scared by the Story of "Midnight Song"

Xinhua Company's second production, "Midnight Song," is a sad and terrifying sound music epic. Yesterday afternoon at 5:00 pm, the story of the play was told at the company's photography studio. The main actors in the play, such as Hu Ping, Gu Eryi, Gu Menghao, Shi Chao, Li Mingjian, Li Junqing, Chen Yun, etc., all came to listen to the lecture. When director Ma Xuweibang spoke to the exciting part, all the actors and staff present had a psychological fear and listened attentively. Just as the atmosphere was extremely tense, a thunderbolt suddenly extinguished the electric torch, and the entire scene was plunged into darkness, making it even more gloomy and miserable. Moreover, it happened to be raining heavily, and the thunder roared. The actor Hu Ping cried out in fear, and all the actors and staff on the scene felt as if they were in the play, even more frightened and trembling. A worker then brought a candle, and the hearts of the people were slightly calmed. Suddenly, someone among the female stars screamed again: "There's a monster! There's a monster!" Everyone followed and looked, and saw two huge and unparalleled giant eyes flashing in the corner of the room. For a moment, order was disrupted, and everyone wanted to get up and escape. Fortunately, the heavy rain suddenly stopped and the lights came back on. The so-called giant eyes were actually two top lights in the photography studio playing tricks. A moment of worry and surprise finally subsided. Everyone thought that this unexpected and terrifying atmosphere when the story of the play was told must be a symbol of future success.
